# PART 1
## Setting, Aesthetics
:
## and Tone.

{{imageMaskEdge2,--offset:10cm,--rotation:180
  ![Background image](https://wa-cdn.nyc3.digitaloceanspaces.com/user-data/production/6ea5d061-1dff-454e-83a7-7b83d4546ed4/uploads/images/c01bf51ac60843330493afd305d48c26.webp){position:absolute,bottom:0,left:-55%,height:100%}
}}


\page
## **Introduction to the Setting**

### **The Vestigium World – Concord City and the Floating Islands**
Concord City exists in a world shaped by a cataclysmic past. The **Vestigium World** is all that remains of the once-mighty world-trees, now reduced to floating crystal islands drifting in the void. These islands hold the remnants of civilization, each a different fragment of what was once a great world. Concord City was designed as a **planned settlement**—an attempt to create order amid the chaos following the collapse of the old world. Its architecture and infrastructure reflect that intent, built not for beauty but for function, with rigid zoning and tiered districts to separate the corporate elite from the struggling masses. The city's economy is driven by finance, trade, and research into the anomalies left behind from the old world’s destruction.

### **What is Concord City?**
Concord City is a sprawling **brutalist metropolis**, an economic and political hub controlled by **corporate entities, bureaucratic inertia, and decayed affluence**. It is a city of contradictions—highly regulated yet filled with lawless underground factions, technologically stagnant yet infused with paranormal anomalies. The streets are lined with old concrete buildings, flickering neon signs, and propaganda billboards reinforcing corporate dominance. While the city is in visible decay, its corporate masters maintain the illusion of control, ensuring that life continues under a rigid, bureaucratic structure. Here, survival is dictated by who you work for, who you owe, and what secrets you can leverage.

### **Aesthetics and Themes**
Concord City embodies **1970s corporate stagnation, brutalist architecture, and a low-tech, high-surveillance dystopia**. Unlike traditional cyberpunk, which features sleek neon streets and advanced technology, Concord City is weighed down by **analog technology, outdated mainframes, and a bureaucratic machine that refuses to evolve**. The paranormal is omnipresent but mundane, its influence hidden within everyday life—anomalous distortions ignored or quietly managed by the system. Corporate propaganda saturates the city, reinforcing themes of control, compliance, and the illusion of stability, while underground movements struggle to expose the truth.

### **What is The Emergence?**
The **Emergence** was a defining moment in Concord City's history—a massive, unexplained event in which thousands of humans appeared in the city overnight. Their sudden presence threw the city into chaos, igniting riots, societal upheaval, and mass paranoia. At the same time, three **colossal faces** manifested in the sky, unleashing destruction before vanishing just as mysteriously. This event triggered a wave of **paranormal anomalies**, some of which continue to shape the city's reality today. Though time has passed, the origins of The Emergence remain unknown, and the city's elite continue to suppress discussions about its true nature. Meanwhile, certain individuals have developed unexplained abilities, further complicating the balance of power.

### **What is A.S.T.R.A.L.?**
A.S.T.R.A.L. (**Agence de Surveillance et de Traitement des Réalités et des Anomalies Localisées**) is the shadowy government agency tasked with **investigating, containing, and managing paranormal phenomena** in Concord City. While the public acknowledges A.S.T.R.A.L.’s existence, its true scope and authority remain obscured. Officially, it is just an investigative body, but in reality, A.S.T.R.A.L. wields near-unlimited power when dealing with anomalies. They enforce strict regulations on the use of paranormal abilities, contain dangerous manifestations, and erase knowledge that threatens corporate stability. Whispers in the underground suggest that A.S.T.R.A.L. is hiding the truth about The Emergence, guarding secrets that could upend the fragile status quo.

### **Who Will You Be?**
This is a world where **truth is dangerous**, where the divide between reality and the unknown is thinner than it seems.  

- A **corporate enforcer** clawing your way to the top?  
- A **paranormal investigator** seeking to unravel the mysteries left behind by The Emergence?  
- A **rogue operator** in the black market, dealing in forbidden knowledge?  
- Or something else entirely?  

Concord City is waiting.  

**But the past never stays buried.**

## **Barbarian**  
*Paranormal Overcharge | Street Brawler | Enforcer | Anomaly*  

> *"They say I lose control when I fight. I say control was never mine to begin with."*  
> — **Brahma, Hollow Chain Enforcer**  

### **Thematic Overview**  
Barbarians in Concord City are anomalies of pure aggression, drawing strength from raw paranormal surges, street brawling, or combat stimulants. They might be the result of failed Thaumatech experiments, cybernetic rejection, or deep-seated trauma that manifests as supernatural rage.
- Some serve as underground gladiators, mercenaries, or street enforcers.  
- Others are unpredictable paranormals, causing havoc in uncontrolled bursts.  
- Their "rage" is a form of paranormal overcharge, adrenaline surge, or reality distortion.  
- Many operate outside corporate law, though some are weaponized by factions.  

### **Creating a Barbarian**  
- Were you a corporate test subject who gained unstable power?  
- Did you grow up in the brutal streets of Concord City, forced to fight to survive?  
- What drives your rage—revenge, justice, self-preservation, or the thrill of combat?  

---

## **Class Features**  
As a **Barbarian**, you gain the following class features.

### **Hit Points**  
- **Hit Dice:** *1d12 per Barbarian level*  
- **Hit Points at 1st Level:** *12 + Constitution modifier*  
- **Hit Points at Higher Levels:** *1d12 (or 7) + Constitution modifier per level after 1st*  

### **Proficiencies**  
- **Armor:** *Light armor, medium armor, shields*  
- **Weapons:** *Simple weapons, martial weapons*  
- **Tools:** *None*  
- **Saving Throws:** *Strength, Constitution*  
- **Skills:** *Choose two from Animal Handling, Athletics, Intimidation, Nature, Perception, and Survival*  

### **Equipment**  
You start with the following equipment, in addition to any granted by your background:  
- *(a)* a two-handed weapon or *(b)* a pair of batons  
- *(a)* an armored jacket or *(b)* a reinforced vest  
- *(a)* an explorer's pack or *(b)* a survival kit  

---

## **Class Table**  
| Level | Proficiency Bonus | Features |  
|:-:|:-:|:--|  
| 1st | +2 | Rage, Unarmored Defense |  
| 2nd | +2 | Reckless Attack, Danger Sense |  
| 3rd | +2 | Primal Path |  
| 4th | +2 | Ability Score Improvement |  
| 5th | +3 | Extra Attack, Fast Movement |  
| 6th | +3 | Primal Path Feature |  
| 7th | +3 | Feral Instinct |  
| 8th | +3 | Ability Score Improvement |

| 15th | +5 | Persistent Rage |

| 19th | +6 | Ability Score Improvement |  
| 20th | +6 | Primal Champion |  

---
\page

## **Class Abilities**  
### **Rage (Level 1)**  
You can tap into an unnatural wellspring of power. On your turn, you can enter a **Rage** as a bonus action. While raging:  
- You have advantage on Strength checks and Strength saving throws.  
- You gain a bonus to melee damage rolls based on your level.  
- You have resistance to bludgeoning, piercing, and slashing damage.  
- Your Rage lasts for 1 minute or until you are knocked unconscious.  
- You can Rage a number of times equal to your **Constitution modifier + 1** (minimum 2) before needing a long rest.  

### **Unarmored Defense (Level 1)**  
When you are not wearing armor, your AC equals **10 + Dexterity modifier + Constitution modifier**. You can use a shield and still gain this benefit.  

### **Reckless Attack (Level 2)**  
When you make your first attack on your turn, you can choose to attack recklessly. Doing so gives you **advantage on melee weapon attack rolls**, but attack rolls against you also have advantage until your next turn.  

### **Danger Sense (Level 2)**  
You gain **advantage on Dexterity saving throws** against effects that you can see, such as traps and spells. You must not be blinded, deafened, or incapacitated to gain this benefit.  


## **Subclasses: Paths of the Barbarian**  
At **3rd level**, barbarians choose a primal path that defines how they channel their rage.

---

Barbarians in Concord City are not primitive warriors but brutal enforcers, cybernetic berserkers, or victims of The Emergence. Their rage is fueled by urban warfare, corporate control, and the scars of a broken world.

### **Path of the Enforcer**
*“Obey, or I’ll make you.”*

#### **Features & Playstyle**
- Specializes in **brutal takedowns, intimidation, and subduing targets**.
- Rage is a **cold, calculated enforcement tool**, rather than uncontrolled fury.
- **Often hired by corporations, gangs, or debt collectors** to ensure obedience.

#### **Subclass Abilities**
| Level | Feature |
|-------|---------|
| 3rd | **Tactical Brutality** – Gain advantage on Intimidation checks, and your rage allows you to grapple and shove creatures more effectively. |
| 6th | **Corporate Authority** – While raging, you can ignore non-magical difficult terrain, and creatures you reduce to 0 HP fall unconscious instead of dying. |
| 10th | **Crowd Control** – When you hit a creature with a melee attack while raging, you can force another enemy within 10 feet to make a Wisdom saving throw or be frightened of you for 1 round. |
| 14th | **Unstoppable Enforcer** – You can use your reaction to halve incoming bludgeoning, piercing, or slashing damage. Your rage now prevents you from being charmed or frightened. |

---

### **Path of the Berserk Machine**
*“Override protocols engaged. Excessive force authorized.”*

#### **Features & Playstyle**
- **Cybernetic enhancements activate during rage**, boosting speed, durability, and combat efficiency.
- Risk of **glitches, overclocking failures, or system errors** during prolonged battle.
- Often **ex-military, escaped test subjects, or corporate black ops agents**.

#### **Subclass Abilities**
| Level | Feature |
|-------|---------|
| 3rd | **Overclocked Reflexes** – Gain a +10 ft. bonus to movement and advantage on Dexterity saving throws while raging. |
| 6th | **Synthetic Adrenaline** – When you reduce a creature to 0 HP, you regain temporary HP equal to your Constitution modifier + your barbarian level. |
| 10th | **Combat HUD** – Gain blindsight 10 feet while raging, and once per long rest, you can automatically reroll an attack roll, ability check, or saving throw. |
| 14th | **System Override** – You can push your cybernetics past their limits, doubling your Strength score for 1 minute. When this ends, you suffer 2 levels of exhaustion. |

### **Path of the Hollowed**
*“I survived The Emergence. But I didn’t come back normal.”*

#### **Features & Playstyle**
- Exposure to **anomalies and unstable energies** has permanently altered you.
- Your rage causes **flickering distortions, spatial warping, or unnatural resilience**.
- Some fear that **you are no longer entirely human**.
\page

#### **Subclass Abilities**
| Level | Feature |
|-------|---------|
| 3rd | **Flickering Form** – While raging, you have a 20% chance each round to blur, causing attacks against you to have disadvantage. |
| 6th | **Warped Resilience** – Gain resistance to force damage, and when you take psychic damage, roll 1d6 to reduce the damage taken. |
| 10th | **Temporal Echo** – Once per long rest, when you drop to 0 HP, you rewind time by 6 seconds, restoring you to half your hit point maximum instead. |
| 14th | **Unstable Phase** – While raging, you can move through creatures and objects as if they were difficult terrain. If you end your turn inside an object, you take 4d10 force damage. |


### **Path of the Blood Debt**
*“They took everything from me. Now I take it back in blood.”*

#### **Features & Playstyle**
- **Fury fueled by personal loss, revenge, or unpaid debts**.
- The closer to death you are, the **stronger and more relentless** you become.
- Common among **gang enforcers, pit fighters, and mercenary warlords**.

#### **Subclass Abilities**
| Level | Feature |
|-------|---------|
| 3rd | **Bloodied Fury** – When you are below half your hit points, your melee attacks deal additional damage equal to your Constitution modifier. |
| 6th | **Undying Wrath** – When reduced to 0 HP, you can make one final attack before falling unconscious. Once per long rest, you can instead drop to 1 HP instead of 0. |
| 10th | **Retribution Strike** – When an enemy reduces one of your allies to 0 HP within 30 feet, you can move up to your speed and make an attack against that enemy as a reaction. |
| 14th | **Relentless Vendetta** – If you have taken damage in the last round, your attacks gain advantage against the creature that harmed you. Additionally, when you drop an enemy to 0 HP, you can immediately move and attack another target. |

---

### **Path of the Rabid**
*"It starts with a bite. It ends with the world in red."*

#### **Features & Playstyle**
- **Rage manifests as an uncontrollable, infectious frenzy.**
- Attacks become **feral**, spreading **madness and panic**.
- Common among **quarantined survivors, failed experiments, and berserk cultists.**

#### **Subclass Abilities**
| Level | Feature |
|-------|---------|
| 3rd | **Feral Surge** – When you enter a rage, you must immediately make an unarmed attack (bite, claw, or fist). If it hits, the target takes necrotic damage equal to your Constitution modifier. |
| 6th | **Contagious Fury** – When you reduce a creature to 0 HP, they convulse violently, forcing an adjacent enemy to make a Wisdom saving throw or enter a temporary rage, attacking their nearest ally. |
| 10th | **Hunger Unleashed** – While raging, when you reduce a creature to 0 HP, you gain temporary HP equal to their Constitution score. You can now rage even if you are at 0 HP—death saving throws only occur after your rage ends. |
| 14th | **Endless Epidemic** – Once per long rest, when reduced to 0 HP, you instead stay active for 1 minute, ignoring all damage and making attacks with advantage. At the end of this duration, you drop to 1 HP and gain one level of exhaustion. |

---

### **Path of the Riot**
*"The city burns, and I’m just getting started."*

#### **Features & Playstyle**
- Thrives in **violent uprisings, urban destruction, and gang warfare**.
- **Improvised weapons and street fighting** define its combat style.
- Common among **revolutionaries, anarchists, and riot enforcers**.

#### **Subclass Abilities**
| Level | Feature |
|-------|---------|
| 3rd | **Street Fighter** – Gain proficiency with improvised weapons (bottles, chairs, bricks). While raging, you gain advantage on attack rolls against armored opponents. |
| 6th | **Fury of the Crowd** – When at least two creatures (allies or enemies) are within 10 feet of you, you can use your reaction to make an additional attack. If an ally is knocked prone, you can retaliate immediately. |
| 10th | **Break the Chains** – You can smash through walls, doors, and barricades as if they were difficult terrain. You gain advantage on Strength checks to escape grapples and restraints. |
| 14th | **Final Stand** – Once per long rest, if you drop to 0 HP while surrounded by three or more enemies, you immediately regain half your HP and rage again. Your rage lasts until all enemies within 30 feet are defeated or fleeing. |

---

\page
### **Path of the Revenant**
*"I already died once. I’m not making that mistake again."*

#### **Features & Playstyle**
- **Refuses to die, fueled by supernatural endurance.**
- Rage enhances **resistance, retaliation, and undying will.**
- Common among **survivors of failed executions, undead berserkers, and lost souls.**

#### **Subclass Abilities**
| Level | Feature |
|-------|---------|
| 3rd | **Undying Rage** – If you fall below half HP while raging, you gain resistance to all damage until your rage ends. If reduced to 0 HP, you can make a Constitution saving throw (DC 10 + half the damage taken) to remain at 1 HP. |
| 6th | **Flesh of the Dead** – You no longer suffer penalties from exhaustion. You are immune to disease, being frightened, and being paralyzed. |
| 10th | **Revenant’s Retaliation** – When you take damage while raging, your attacker takes psychic damage equal to your Barbarian level. If an enemy reduces you to 0 HP, you may make a single melee attack against them before falling. |
| 14th | **Deathless Charge** – Once per long rest, when reduced to 0 HP, you instead regain half your HP and immediately take your turn again. For the next minute, you cannot be knocked unconscious unless reduced to negative HP equal to your max HP. |

---

### **Path of the Inferno**
*"Some men just want to watch the world burn. I’m one of them."*

#### **Features & Playstyle**
- **Rage manifests as pure fire**, burning enemies and fueling destruction.
- Gains **flame-based resilience and devastating fire attacks**.
- Common among **pyromaniacs, industrial saboteurs, and zealots of destruction.**

#### **Subclass Abilities**
| Level | Feature |
|-------|---------|
| 3rd | **Burning Blood** – While raging, any creature that strikes you in melee takes fire damage equal to your Strength modifier. If you take fire damage, you heal half that amount instead. |
| 6th | **Fury of the Blaze** – When you reduce a creature to 0 HP, they erupt in flames, dealing 2d6 fire damage to all enemies within 10 feet. Fire does not harm your equipment or clothing. |
| 10th | **Ash and Ruin** – You can walk through fire and hazardous environments without penalty. If an enemy is on fire, your attacks automatically deal extra fire damage equal to your Barbarian level. |
| 14th | **Final Ember** – Once per long rest, you may ignite yourself into a living inferno. Enemies within 5 feet take 2d8 fire damage each round. If reduced to 0 HP, you explode, dealing 4d10 fire damage in a 30-foot radius. |


---
### **Path of the Scourge**
*"I am not here to fight. I am here to punish."*

#### **Features & Playstyle**
- **Specializes in punishing enemies with unavoidable suffering.**
- Rage is fueled by **revenge, interrogation, or enforcing pain.**
- Common among **mercenary executioners, torturers, and prison enforcers.**

#### **Subclass Abilities**
| Level | Feature |
|-------|---------|
| 3rd | **Marked for Pain** – When you hit an enemy, you can mark them for suffering. Marked creatures take additional necrotic damage equal to your Rage bonus and cannot regain HP until your rage ends. |
| 6th | **Punishment in Blood** – When a marked enemy takes damage, you can use your reaction to force them to make a Constitution saving throw (DC 8 + your proficiency + Strength modifier) or take additional necrotic damage. |
| 10th | **Chain of Suffering** – If you reduce a marked enemy to 0 HP, you may immediately mark another enemy within 10 feet as a free action. If reduced to half HP, your rage extends by 1 minute. |
| 14th | **The Final Judgment** – Once per long rest, you unleash an aura of punishment. Enemies within 30 feet have disadvantage on saving throws against fear and necrotic damage. Marked enemies take double your Rage damage bonus. If you reduce an enemy to 0 HP, their body is reduced to ash and cannot be revived except by a 9th-level spell. |

\page

## **Multiclassing**  
If your campaign allows multiclassing, use the following rules for a **Barbarian** multiclass character.  

### **Ability Score Minimums**  
- Strength 13  

### **Proficiencies Gained**  
- Light armor, medium armor, shields, simple weapons, martial weapons  

---

## **Quick Build**  
You can make a **Barbarian** quickly by following these suggestions:  
- Choose **Orc or Human** for a strong thematic fit.  
- Pick the **Criminal Enforcer** or **Gladiator** background.  
- Prioritize **Strength and Constitution**.  
- Take a two-handed melee weapon and light armor for maximum efficiency.

## **Bard**  
*Corporate Fixer | Media Manipulator | Underground Performer | Paranormal Storyteller*  

> *"The right words can move mountains. Or burn bridges."*  
> — **Isolde "Jack Rouge" Faure, The Free Syndicate**  

### **Thematic Overview**  
Bards in Concord City are masters of persuasion, performance, and information warfare. They manipulate narratives, bend the will of others, and shape reality with their words. Some serve as corporate propagandists, others as underground truth-seekers, and a few tap into the lost echoes of The Emergence to fuel their paranormal abilities.
- Bards specialize in **social engineering, performance, and subtle reality manipulation**.  
- Some work in **corporate PR or high-end entertainment**, controlling public perception.  
- Others operate as **whistleblowers, underground journalists, or black-market information brokers**.  
- Paranormal bards channel **the lingering voices of The Emergence**, giving them eerie knowledge and influence.  

### **Creating a Bard**  
- Did you come from the entertainment industry, the corporate world, or the underground media?  
- What is your chosen medium—music, storytelling, digital media, or old-fashioned persuasion?  
- Do you serve a cause, or are you purely in it for personal gain?  


## **Class Features**  
As a **Bard**, you gain the following class features.

### **Hit Points**  
- **Hit Dice:** *1d8 per Bard level*  
- **Hit Points at 1st Level:** *8 + Constitution modifier*  
- **Hit Points at Higher Levels:** *1d8 (or 5) + Constitution modifier per level after 1st*  

### **Proficiencies**  
- **Armor:** *Light armor*  
- **Weapons:** *Simple weapons, hand crossbows, longswords, rapiers, short swords*  
- **Tools:** *Three musical instruments or digital media tools of your choice*  
- **Saving Throws:** *Dexterity, Charisma*  
- **Skills:** *Choose any three*  

### **Equipment**  
You start with the following equipment, in addition to any granted by your background:  
- *(a)* a rapier or *(b)* a sidearm with 10 rounds  
- *(a)* a diplomat’s pack or *(b)* an entertainer’s pack  
- *(a)* a digital audio interface or *(b)* a traditional musical instrument  
- A concealed microphone or media device  


## **Class Table**  
| Level | Proficiency Bonus | Features |  
|:-:|:-:|:--|  
| 1st | +2 | Bardic Inspiration (d6), Spellcasting |  
| 2nd | +2 | Jack of All Trades, Song of Rest (d6) |  
| 3rd | +2 | Bard College, Expertise |  
| 4th | +2 | Ability Score Improvement |  
| 5th | +3 | Bardic Inspiration (d8), Font of Inspiration |  
| 6th | +3 | Countercharm, Bard College Feature |  
| 7th | +3 | Additional Expertise |  
| 8th | +3 | Ability Score Improvement |  
| 9th | +4 | Song of Rest (d8) |  
| 10th | +4 | Bardic Inspiration (d10), Magical Secrets |  
| 11th | +4 | Bard College Feature |  
| 12th | +4 | Ability Score Improvement |  
| 13th | +5 | Song of Rest (d10) |  
| 14th | +5 | Magical Secrets |  
| 15th | +5 | Bardic Inspiration (d12) |  
| 16th | +5 | Ability Score Improvement |  
| 17th | +6 | Song of Rest (d12) |  
| 18th | +6 | Magical Secrets |  
| 19th | +6 | Ability Score Improvement |  
| 20th | +6 | Superior Inspiration |  

---
\page
## **Class Abilities**  
### **Bardic Inspiration (Level 1)**  
You can inspire others through your words, performance, or digital broadcasts. As a bonus action, you grant one creature a **Bardic Inspiration die (d6)**. They can add this die to an ability check, attack roll, or saving throw. This die increases at higher levels.  

### **Jack of All Trades (Level 2)**  
You can add half your proficiency bonus (rounded down) to any ability check you make that doesn't already include your proficiency bonus.  

### **Song of Rest (Level 2)**  
During a short rest, you and your allies regain an extra **d6 hit points** when healing. This die increases at higher levels.  

### **Expertise (Level 3)**  
Choose two skill proficiencies. Your proficiency bonus is doubled for any ability check that uses those skills. At level 10, choose two more.  


---

## **Multiclassing**  
If your campaign allows multiclassing, use the following rules for a **Bard** multiclass character.  

### **Ability Score Minimums**  
- Charisma 13  

### **Proficiencies Gained**  
- One skill of your choice, one musical instrument or media tool  

---

## **Quick Build**  
You can make a **Bard** quickly by following these suggestions:  
- Choose **Tiefling or Elf** for a strong thematic fit.  
- Pick the **Entertainer** or **Charlatan** background.  
- Prioritize **Charisma**, followed by **Dexterity**.  
- Take a rapier and a musical instrument or digital recording device for optimal roleplay potential.  


## **Subclasses: Bard Colleges**  
At **3rd level**, you choose a college that shapes your skills. Choose from the following options:  

## College of Influence  
*"You don’t need power if you control the people who have it."*  

### **The Concept**  
Bards of the **College of Influence** are not mere performers—they are **social engineers.** They weave **narratives, manipulate crowds, and control the flow of information.** Whether corporate consultants or underground agitators, they know that **words shape reality.**  

### **Corporate Charisma** *(3rd level)*  
You gain proficiency in **Deception and Persuasion** if you don’t already have them. Additionally, you can use **Bardic Inspiration** to make an ally’s next Persuasion or Deception check **automatically succeed** against creatures with an Intelligence score lower than yours.  

### **Targeted Messaging** *(6th level)*  
When you use **Bardic Inspiration**, you may also transmit **a subliminal command.**  
- The target must make a **Wisdom saving throw.**  
- On a failure, they **repeat a phrase, belief, or idea you implant.**  
- Anyone who hears it must make a **Wisdom saving throw** or begin **believing it as fact** for the next hour.  

### **Mass Rebranding** *(14th level)*  
You can **rewrite an event in real-time.**  
- As an action, **up to 10 creatures within 120 feet** must make an **Intelligence saving throw.**  
- On a failure, they believe your version of events **is the only truth.**  
- Attempts to challenge your version **automatically have disadvantage.**  

---

## College of Pop  
*"It’s not about the song. It’s about making sure everyone hears it."*  

### **The Concept**  
Pop bards **manufacture obsession.** They **don’t just perform—they become part of culture itself.** Whether as **corporate-backed icons or underground viral sensations,** they shape trends and create **undeniable movements.**  

### **Hooked on the Sound** *(3rd level)*  
When you perform for **at least 1 minute**, creatures who hear you must make a **Charisma saving throw.**  
- On a failure, they become **fixated on you**, finding you **irresistibly compelling** for the next hour.  
- While fixated, they have **disadvantage on checks to resist your influence.**  
\page

### **Cultural Saturation** *(6th level)*  
You gain **advantage on Persuasion checks** when speaking to groups of **five or more.** Additionally, when you **use Bardic Inspiration**, you may affect **two creatures instead of one.**  

### **Industry Plant** *(14th level)*  
Once per long rest, you can **force a failed social interaction to be erased from public memory.**  
- Affected creatures must make a **Wisdom saving throw.**  
- On a failure, **they remember the event in the way most favorable to you.**  

---

## College of Silence  
*"The most powerful voices are the ones you never hear."*  

### **The Concept**  
Bards of the **College of Silence** understand that words can **erase as well as inspire.** They manipulate **what isn’t said, what isn’t recorded, and what is deliberately forgotten.**  

### **Erased Presence** *(3rd level)*  
You can use **Bardic Inspiration** to suppress a creature’s presence.  
- They leave **no sound, no recorded trace, and no written memory** for the next 10 minutes.  
- Security cameras glitch when looking at them.  
- Attempts to recall them later **result in incomplete memories.**  

### **Dead Air** *(6th level)*  
When casting a spell with verbal components, you can instead **erase sound entirely.**  
- The spell is cast **silently**, and cannot be overheard.  
- All sound within **a 10-foot radius** of you ceases until the end of your next turn.  

### **Unperson Protocol** *(14th level)*  
Once per long rest, you may **erase a person from a social space.**  
- As an action, **one creature within 60 feet** must make a **Charisma saving throw.**  
- On a failure, **everyone in the area** ignores them as if they were never there **for 1 hour.**  
- The effect ends if they take damage **or forcefully interact with the world.**  

---

### **College of Bureaucracy**  
*"Paperwork is just another form of spellcasting."*  

#### **Features & Playstyle**  
- **Masters of legal manipulation, procedural delays, and administrative dominance.**  
- Turns **bureaucracy into a form of combat.**  
- Common among **corporate lawyers, compliance enforcers, and regulation agents.**  

#### **Subclass Abilities**  
| Level | Feature |  
|-------|---------|  
| 3rd | **Procedural Delay** – You can use Bardic Inspiration to enforce a legal delay, preventing an enemy from acting for 1 round due to “improper authorization.” |  
| 6th | **Red Tape Mastery** – If an enemy tries to attack, arrest, or interrogate you, they must make a Charisma save or be delayed for 1d4 minutes due to “pending paperwork.” |  
| 14th | **Weaponized Legalese** – Once per long rest, you can present a legal argument that forces creatures to follow your direction, believing they are contractually obligated. |  

---

### **College of Nightlife**  
*"The party never ends, but the people do."*  

#### **Features & Playstyle**  
- **Masters of distraction, euphoria, and controlling social settings.**  
- Performances turn into **hypnotic, uncontrollable experiences.**  
- Common among **club DJs, underground movement leaders, and high-profile entertainers.**  

#### **Subclass Abilities**  
| Level | Feature |  
|-------|---------|  
| 3rd | **Rhythmic Momentum** – While in a club or large crowd, gain +10 movement speed and advantage on Dexterity saves. |  
| 6th | **Euphoric Performance** – After performing for 1 minute, creatures must make a Wisdom save or fall into a euphoric trance for 10 minutes, failing to perceive danger. |  
| 14th | **The Rave Never Ends** – You and allies within 60 feet ignore exhaustion, fear, and death saves for 1 hour as long as music plays. |  

---

## **College of Escorts**  
*"Pleasure is a transaction, and I always get paid."*  

#### **Features & Playstyle**  
- **Uses charm, seduction, and emotional control to influence others.**  
- Gains power through **one-on-one interactions and intimate persuasion.**  
- Common among **courtesans, spies, and high-end socialites.**  

\page

#### **Subclass Abilities**  
| Level | Feature |  
|-------|---------|  
| 3rd | **Disarming Presence** – Gain advantage on Persuasion and Insight checks when engaging someone directly. Using Bardic Inspiration can impose disadvantage on an enemy’s next attack against you. |  
| 6th | **Entrancing Touch** – By touching a creature, you can force a Wisdom saving throw. On failure, they experience a **heightened emotional connection** for 10 minutes. |  
| 14th | **The Final Embrace** – Once per long rest, you can charm a creature for 10 minutes, causing them to view you as **the most important person in their life.** |  

---

#### **College of Street Performance**  
*"The city is my stage, and the people are my audience."*  

#### **Features & Playstyle**  
- **Masters of performing in public spaces and shifting mass perception.**  
- Blends in effortlessly with **urban crowds and street culture.**  
- Common among **buskers, political agitators, and social revolutionaries.**  

#### **Subclass Abilities**  
| Level | Feature |  
|-------|---------|  
| 3rd | **Crowd Control** – Gain advantage on Performance checks in public. If at least 5 people are watching, you can use Bardic Inspiration without expending a die. |  
| 6th | **Urban Camouflage** – You can blend into a crowd, allowing you to Hide as a bonus action in populated areas. |  
| 14th | **The People's Champion** – Once per long rest, you can perform in a way that makes all nearby citizens view you as an ally for 1 hour. |  

---

### **College of Wanderlust**  
*"No home, no master, no chains."*  

#### **Features & Playstyle**  
- **Masters of travel, storytelling, and spreading folklore.**  
- Blends myth and reality into **a constantly evolving legend.**  
- Common among **travelers, exiles, and rogue storytellers.**  

#### **Subclass Abilities**  
| Level | Feature |  
|-------|---------|  
| 3rd | **Pathfinder’s Instinct** – You can never become lost and can always sense the quickest route out of any area. |  
| 6th | **Rolling Inspiration** – Allies using your Bardic Inspiration can immediately move up to half their speed without provoking opportunity attacks. |  
| 14th | **Folk Legend** – Once per long rest, you can make it so that a settlement **already knows your reputation**, causing them to fear, admire, or welcome you. |  

---

### **College of Depression**  
*"I sing for the ones who can’t anymore."*  

#### **Features & Playstyle**  
- **Masters of sorrowful ballads, shared pain, and overwhelming emotion.**  
- Their music is **too real for some to handle.**  
- Common among **mourners, lost souls, and those who suffer for others.**  

#### **Subclass Abilities**  
| Level | Feature |  
|-------|---------|  
| 3rd | **Melancholy Ballad** – Creatures that hear your performance must make a Wisdom save or become emotionally overwhelmed, imposing disadvantage on attack rolls and ability checks for 1 minute. |  
| 6th | **Shared Pain** – When an ally within 30 feet takes damage, you can choose to take half of it instead. You also gain temporary HP equal to half your Bard level. |  
| 14th | **The Weight of the World** – Once per long rest, you can force a creature to feel overwhelming despair. They must make a Charisma save or collapse, unable to act for 1 minute. |  

---


### **College of Ska**  
*"You can’t be sad if you’re skanking fast enough."*  

#### **Features & Playstyle**  
- **Masters of relentless rhythm, speed, and chaotic momentum.**  
- Uses **upbeat energy to prevent exhaustion, fear, and despair.**  
- Common among **punk revolutionaries, underground musicians, and street performers.**  

#### **Subclass Abilities**  
| Level | Feature |  
|-------|---------|  
| 3rd | **Upbeat Resistance** – Gain advantage on saving throws against charm and fear effects. Whenever you take damage, you can immediately use Bardic Inspiration as a reaction. |  
| 6th | **Ska Breakdown** – As an action, all enemies within 30 feet must make a Dexterity save or be knocked prone by the sheer energy of your performance. |  
| 14th | **Unstoppable Beat** – Once per long rest, you can grant all allies within 60 feet immunity to exhaustion, fear, and paralysis for 1 hour. If they would drop to 0 HP, they remain at 1 HP until the effect ends. |

## **Cleric**  
*Paranormal Cultist | Corporate Chaplain | Anomaly Researcher | Prophet of the Beyond*  

> *"The gods are silent. But something else listens."*  
> — **Elder Laurent Cassiel, Dawnkeepers**  

### **Thematic Overview**  
Clerics in Concord City do not serve traditional gods. Instead, they are conduits for **paranormal entities, forgotten forces, or ideological movements**. Some work for corporate think tanks, wielding supernatural authority in boardrooms. Others belong to radical cults, drawing power from entities awakened during The Emergence.
- Clerics are **agents of the unknown**, wielding faith-based or ideological power.  
- Some work as **A.S.T.R.A.L. researchers**, attempting to harness anomalies.  
- Others are **members of secret cults**, serving forgotten entities.  
- A few act as **corporate chaplains**, using faith as a tool of control or comfort.  

### **Creating a Cleric**  
- Do you draw power from faith, ideology, or an otherworldly patron?  
- Were you trained in a corporate institution, or did you experience an awakening?  
- What is your mission—healing, control, enlightenment, or destruction?  

---

## **Class Features**  
As a **Cleric**, you gain the following class features.

### **Hit Points**  
- **Hit Dice:** *1d8 per Cleric level*  
- **Hit Points at 1st Level:** *8 + Constitution modifier*  
- **Hit Points at Higher Levels:** *1d8 (or 5) + Constitution modifier per level after 1st*  

### **Proficiencies**  
- **Armor:** *Light armor, medium armor, shields*  
- **Weapons:** *Simple weapons*  
- **Tools:** *None*  
- **Saving Throws:** *Wisdom, Charisma*  
- **Skills:** *Choose two from History, Insight, Medicine, Persuasion, and Religion*  

### **Equipment**  
You start with the following equipment, in addition to any granted by your background:  
- *(a)* a tactical baton or *(b)* a sidearm with 10 rounds  
- *(a)* a reinforced clerical robe or *(b)* an armored vest  
- *(a)* a corporate dossier or *(b)* a set of ritual scrolls  
- A diagnostic scanner or occult sensor  

---

## **Class Table**  
| Level | Proficiency Bonus | Features |  
|:-:|:-:|:--|  
| 1st | +2 | Spellcasting, Divine Domain |  
| 2nd | +2 | Channel Divinity (1/rest), Divine Domain Feature |  
| 3rd | +2 | Channel Divinity (2/rest) |  
| 4th | +2 | Ability Score Improvement |  
| 5th | +3 | Destroy Undead (CR 1/2) |  
| 6th | +3 | Divine Domain Feature |  
| 7th | +3 | Channel Divinity (3/rest) |  
| 8th | +3 | Ability Score Improvement, Destroy Undead (CR 1) |  
| 9th | +4 | - |  
| 10th | +4 | Divine Intervention |  
| 11th | +4 | Destroy Undead (CR 2) |  
| 12th | +4 | Ability Score Improvement |  
| 13th | +5 | - |  
| 14th | +5 | Destroy Undead (CR 3) |  
| 15th | +5 | - |  
| 16th | +5 | Ability Score Improvement |  
| 17th | +6 | Destroy Undead (CR 4), Divine Domain Feature |  
| 18th | +6 | Channel Divinity (4/rest) |  
| 19th | +6 | Ability Score Improvement |  
| 20th | +6 | Divine Intervention Improvement |  

---
\page

## **Class Abilities**  
### **Spellcasting (Level 1)**  
Your connection to **paranormal forces** allows you to cast spells. See the Cleric spell list for available options.

### **Divine Domain (Level 1)**  
Choose a domain that reflects your faith or ideology. Your domain grants you additional spells and features at **1st, 2nd, 6th, 8th, and 17th level**.

### **Channel Divinity (Level 2)**  
You can channel your power into a supernatural effect. You start with one option, gaining more through your **Divine Domain**.
- **Turn the Unholy:** You force supernatural entities to flee in fear.  
- **Corporate Command:** Issue a supernatural decree, compelling a target to obey.  


## Cleric Domains  

---

### **Domain of Contracts**  
*"Sign here, and I’ll make sure you get what you deserve."*  

#### **Features & Playstyle**  
- **Wields legal binding agreements as divine power.**  
- Focuses on **manipulation, enforcement, and inescapable oaths.**  
- Common among **corporate priests, law enforcers, and legal arbiters.**  

#### **Domain Abilities**  
| Level | Feature |  
|-------|---------|  
| 1st | **Binding Clause** – You can cast *Command* without expending a spell slot once per long rest. |  
| 2nd | **Channel Divinity: Contractual Obligation** – Force a creature to sign a supernatural contract. They must make a Wisdom saving throw or be magically bound to follow one directive for 24 hours. |  
| 6th | **Fine Print** – When an enemy targets you with a spell or effect, they must make an Intelligence saving throw or **suffer their own effect instead.** |  
| 8th | **Divine Authority** – Your spells ignore resistance from creatures that have made a deal or contract within the past week. |  
| 17th | **Immutable Law** – Once per long rest, you can **rewrite the reality of a situation**, forcing any event within the past minute to occur differently. |  

---

### **Domain of Surveillance**  
*"You can’t hide. We see everything."*  

#### **Features & Playstyle**  
- **Focuses on divine observation, tracking, and inescapable surveillance.**  
- Wields **scrying, divine sensors, and mind-reading** to monitor all activities.  
- Common among **corporate spies, government enforcers, and A.S.T.R.A.L. operatives.**  

#### **Domain Abilities**  
| Level | Feature |  
|-------|---------|  
| 1st | **Eyes Everywhere** – You gain *Detect Thoughts* and *Clairvoyance* as domain spells. |  
| 2nd | **Channel Divinity: Surveillance Grid** – For 10 minutes, you can **see through all security cameras and divination spells within 1 mile.** |  
| 6th | **Unavoidable Insight** – You always know when you are being lied to. Your divination spells work on creatures that are otherwise immune to scrying. |  
| 8th | **Data Erasure** – Once per long rest, you can alter or remove a creature’s memory of an event from the last 24 hours. |  
| 17th | **The Eternal Watch** – You no longer need sight to perceive. You always know the locations of creatures within 1 mile of you, unless they are fully erased from existence. |  

---

### **Domain of Anomalies**  
*"The gods are gone. But something else remains."*  

#### **Features & Playstyle**  
- **Channels raw anomalous energy instead of divine power.**  
- Uses **reality distortions, eldritch forces, and glitches** in divine magic.  
- Common among **rogue A.S.T.R.A.L. clerics, forgotten cultists, and scholars of lost anomalies.**  

#### **Domain Abilities**  
| Level | Feature |  
|-------|---------|  
| 1st | **Reality Fracture** – You gain *Misty Step* and *Detect Magic* as domain spells. |  
| 2nd | **Channel Divinity: Break the Pattern** – Once per rest, **negate a magical or supernatural effect**, causing it to glitch out instead of resolving. |  
| 6th | **Unstable Miracles** – When you cast a spell, roll a d6. On a 6, the spell is empowered and deals double damage or healing. On a 1, **unintended effects manifest.** |  
| 8th | **Disruptive Touch** – Your melee attacks **deal extra force damage** and disrupt magical effects within 5 feet. |  
| 17th | **Anomaly Ascendant** – You can **alter one fundamental rule of reality within a 60-foot radius for 1 minute.** This can include changes like *gravity inversion, instant decay, or breaking cause and effect.* |  

\page

### **Domain of the Forgotten**  
*"We remember what the world wants to forget."*  

#### **Features & Playstyle**  
- **Draws power from the fading echoes of gods that once existed.**  
- Uses **memory magic, lost knowledge, and resurrection-like abilities.**  
- Common among **librarians of erased history, ghost-priests, and seekers of the Old Pantheon.**  

#### **Domain Abilities**  
| Level | Feature |  
|-------|---------|  
| 1st | **Whispered Prayers** – Gain *Speak with Dead* and *Legend Lore* as domain spells. |  
| 2nd | **Channel Divinity: Remembrance** – You may ask a question to an erased god or entity. You receive **an answer in cryptic whispers.** |  
| 6th | **Lingering Presence** – Spirits of the forgotten shield you. When you take damage, roll a d6. On a 5 or 6, **you take no damage.** |  
| 8th | **Restore the Vanished** – You can temporarily return an erased entity to existence for 1 minute. |  
| 17th | **Echo of Divinity** – Once per long rest, you can **cast a spell of 9th level, even if you do not have the slot.** The spell is unstable and may have **side effects.** |  

---

### **Domain of Vice**  
*"There is no sin. Only pleasure, power, and profit."*  

#### **Features & Playstyle**  
- **Embraces indulgence, excess, and corruption as divine gifts.**  
- Uses **deception, persuasion, and temptation magic** to manipulate others.  
- Common among **cult leaders, corrupt priests, and underground pleasure brokers.**  

#### **Domain Abilities**  
| Level | Feature |  
|-------|---------|  
| 1st | **All That Glitters** – Gain *Charm Person* and *Suggestion* as domain spells. |  
| 2nd | **Channel Divinity: The Cost of Desire** – Target a creature within 30 feet. They must succeed a Charisma saving throw or become **infatuated** with something they desire, rendering them unable to focus on anything else. |  
| 6th | **Honeyed Words** – You have advantage on Persuasion and Deception checks. Your charm spells last twice as long. |  
| 8th | **Divine Temptation** – Once per long rest, you may **ask a creature to do one action against their morals.** If they fail a Wisdom save, they comply. |  
| 17th | **Master of the Flesh** – You can **control a charmed creature indefinitely**, as long as they remain in your presence. |  

---

### **Domain of The Monarchy**  
*"The crown is divine. You will kneel."*  

#### **Features & Playstyle**  
- **Wields political power as divine right.**  
- Specializes in **control, law, and enforcing hierarchical authority.**  
- Common among **royal advisors, knight-priests, and political enforcers.**  

#### **Domain Abilities**  
| Level | Feature |  
|-------|---------|  
| 1st | **Ruler’s Command** – Gain *Command* and *Hold Person* as domain spells. |  
| 2nd | **Channel Divinity: The Sovereign’s Will** – Target a creature within 30 feet. They must succeed on a Charisma saving throw or be forced to kneel, rendering them prone for 1 minute. |  
| 6th | **Divine Right** – When you make a Persuasion check, you can add your Wisdom modifier to the roll. |  
| 8th | **Unbreakable Law** – You can impose **magical contracts** that force creatures to follow their word. |  
| 17th | **King’s Edict** – Once per long rest, **declare a law that must be followed for the next 24 hours within a 1-mile radius.** |  

---

### **Domain of Industry**  
*"The city never sleeps. Neither do I."*  

#### **Features & Playstyle**  
- **Channels divine energy through labor, production, and mechanical efficiency.**  
- Focuses on **enhancing durability, repairing structures, and enforcing relentless progress.**  
- Common among **factory foremen, corporate engineers, and industrial zealots.**  

#### **Domain Abilities**  
| Level | Feature |  
|-------|---------|  
| 1st | **Built to Last** – Gain proficiency in heavy armor and tools related to construction and engineering. |  
| 2nd | **Channel Divinity: Reinforce** – Choose a creature or object within 30 feet. Until the end of your next turn, it gains resistance to all damage and cannot be moved. |  
| 6th | **Unyielding Efficiency** – You and your allies within 10 feet reduce all exhaustion levels by 1 at the end of a short rest. |  
| 8th | **Divine Fabrication** – Gain the ability to repair broken items instantly or conjure simple machinery at will. |  
| 17th | **Metropolis Ascendant** – Once per long rest, you can invoke the city itself, causing structures to shift at your command, forming bridges, walls, or pathways within a 120-foot radius. |  

\page

### **Domain of The Void**  
*"I hear the silence between the stars."*  

#### **Features & Playstyle**  
- **Worships the concept of absence, void energy, and cosmic negation.**  
- Wields **black-hole magic, antimatter destruction, and existential horror.**  
- Common among **astral cultists, void monks, and those who listen for the Whisperer.**  

#### **Domain Abilities**  
| Level | Feature |  
|-------|---------|  
| 1st | **Voidwalker’s Resilience** – Gain resistance to psychic and necrotic damage. |  
| 2nd | **Channel Divinity: Erasure** – Target a creature or object within 60 feet. They must make a Charisma saving throw or be temporarily phased out of existence until the end of their next turn. |  
| 6th | **Gaze Into Nothing** – Your mind is shielded from mental influence. You are immune to charm, possession, and fear effects. |  
| 8th | **Gravity Distortion** – When you cast a spell, you can create a **10-foot radius zone of zero gravity** for 1 minute. |  
| 17th | **The Final Silence** – Once per long rest, you can **erase a target from existence** for 1 minute. Only divine intervention can restore them before this time passes. |  

---

### **Domain of Pain**  
*"Through suffering, I am made whole."*  

#### **Features & Playstyle**  
- **Gains divine strength through self-inflicted pain and suffering.**  
- Focuses on **endurance, masochistic empowerment, and inflicting agony on others.**  
- Common among **fanatics, torturers, and those who believe in righteous punishment.**  

#### **Domain Abilities**  
| Level | Feature |  
|-------|---------|  
| 1st | **Rite of the Martyr** – When you take damage, you gain temporary HP equal to half the damage received. |  
| 2nd | **Channel Divinity: Shared Agony** – Target a creature within 30 feet. For the next minute, any damage they deal is also inflicted upon them. |  
| 6th | **Pain Tolerance** – While below half HP, you gain resistance to all non-magical damage. |  
| 8th | **Suffering’s Reward** – When you take damage from an attack, you can use your reaction to make a melee attack with advantage. |  
| 17th | **Divine Affliction** – Once per long rest, you can curse an enemy so that every source of healing they receive instead causes them necrotic damage equal to the amount healed. |  

---

### **Domain of The Underground**  
*"Faith doesn’t belong in a church. It belongs in the streets."*  

#### **Features & Playstyle**  
- **Worships the unwritten rules of the city’s underbelly.**  
- Specializes in **stealth, deception, and illicit miracles.**  
- Common among **smugglers, thieves’ guild chaplains, and black-market dealers.**  

#### **Domain Abilities**  
| Level | Feature |  
|-------|---------|  
| 1st | **Low Profile** – Gain proficiency in Deception and Stealth. You can use your holy symbol as a forged identity. |  
| 2nd | **Channel Divinity: Vanish** – You can turn yourself and up to two allies invisible for 1 minute. |  
| 6th | **Divine Smuggling** – You can hide any small object or weapon from magical detection. |  
| 8th | **Whispered Prayers** – When casting healing spells, you do not reveal yourself through divine energy. You leave no magical trace of your work. |  
| 17th | **The City Provides** – Once per long rest, you can declare that an item, weapon, or ally is "already waiting" for you somewhere nearby. The GM must provide a plausible way for you to obtain it within the hour. |  

---

### **Domain of Reclamation**  
*"The city moves on. I bring back what was lost."*  

#### **Features & Playstyle**  
- **Focuses on restoring forgotten places, lost artifacts, and buried secrets.**  
- Wields **divine excavation, object resurrection, and memory restoration.**  
- Common among **urban explorers, restoration priests, and archaeologists of the forgotten.**  

#### **Domain Abilities**  
| Level | Feature |  
|-------|---------|  
| 1st | **Reawaken the Past** – Gain *Identify* and *Mending* as domain spells. |  
| 2nd | **Channel Divinity: Restore** – You may touch a destroyed object or ruined place and see a vision of its last 24 hours before destruction. |  
| 6th | **Vestiges of the Old World** – When standing in a ruin or abandoned area, your spells have their range doubled. |  
| 8th | **The Old Places Remember** – Once per long rest, you can ask a question to the spirit of a building or place, receiving a cryptic answer. |  
| 17th | **Reclaim the Lost** – Once per long rest, you can restore **a ruined location, lost artifact, or missing knowledge**, even if history has forgotten it. |  

\page

### **Domain of the Nameless**  
*"We have no name. We are legion."*  

#### **Features & Playstyle**  
- **Draws power from anonymity, erased history, and hidden records.**  
- Uses **divine obfuscation, identity erasure, and name-stealing abilities.**  
- Common among **spies, erased entities, and those who refuse to be known.**  

#### **Domain Abilities**  
| Level | Feature |  
|-------|---------|  
| 1st | **Mask of the Unknown** – You gain *Disguise Self* and *Pass Without Trace* as domain spells. |  
| 2nd | **Channel Divinity: Forgotten Name** – Target a creature within 60 feet. They must succeed on a Wisdom saving throw or **forget your existence for 1 minute.** |  
| 6th | **Slip Through the Cracks** – If you take no aggressive actions for 1 minute, the world instinctively forgets your presence, making it harder to track you. |  
| 8th | **Unwritten Fate** – Once per long rest, you can **prevent yourself from being remembered** by anyone who sees you for the next hour. |  
| 17th | **The Erased** – You can permanently remove a name from reality, preventing resurrection, scrying, or historical mention of the target. |  

---

## **Multiclassing**  
If your campaign allows multiclassing, use the following rules for a **Cleric** multiclass character.  

### **Ability Score Minimums**  
- Wisdom 13  

### **Proficiencies Gained**  
- Light armor, medium armor, shields  

---

## **Quick Build**  
You can make a **Cleric** quickly by following these suggestions:  
- Choose **Human or Tiefling** for a thematic fit.  
- Pick the **A.S.T.R.A.L. Agent** or **Covenant Preacher** background.  
- Prioritize **Wisdom**, followed by **Charisma**.  
- Take a sidearm and reinforced vest for protection.

## **Druid**  
*Reality Weaver | Paranormal Shaman | Echo of the Old World | Veilwalker*  

> *"Nature? You mean the wreckage of the old world, the ghosts of what once was? I don’t worship the past—I listen to it."*  
> — **Sister Elira, Order of the Hollow Veil**  

### **Thematic Overview**  
Druids in Concord City are not tied to traditional nature. Instead, they tap into **paranormal echoes, remnants of the lost world, and the shifting energies of reality itself**. Some are mystics who commune with **lingering spirits**, while others serve as **keepers of forgotten knowledge** or **protectors of the hidden places** where The Emergence’s scars remain.
- Druids are **weavers of reality, protectors of paranormal anomalies, and guardians of the unknown**.  
- Some work as **A.S.T.R.A.L. investigators**, studying unstable regions of Concord City.  
- Others exist on the fringes, members of **esoteric cults** or nomadic visionaries.  
- Their magic is drawn from **lost memories, supernatural whispers, and eldritch ecosystems**.  

### **Creating a Druid**  
- Do you revere the remnants of the lost world or seek to unravel its secrets?  
- Are you part of a hidden sect, a rogue scholar, or a wanderer who listens to the city’s echoes?  
- What is your connection to The Emergence? Were you changed by it, or do you seek to undo its scars?  


## **Class Features**  
As a **Druid**, you gain the following class features.

### **Hit Points**  
- **Hit Dice:** *1d8 per Druid level*  
- **Hit Points at 1st Level:** *8 + Constitution modifier*  
- **Hit Points at Higher Levels:** *1d8 (or 5) + Constitution modifier per level after 1st*  

### **Proficiencies**  
- **Armor:** *Light armor, medium armor (no metal), shields (no metal)*  
- **Weapons:** *Clubs, daggers, spears, quarterstaffs, scythes*  
- **Tools:** *Alchemical kits, ritual components*  
- **Saving Throws:** *Intelligence, Wisdom*  
- **Skills:** *Choose two from Arcana, Insight, Medicine, Nature, Perception, and Religion*  

### **Equipment**  
You start with the following equipment, in addition to any granted by your background:  
- *(a)* a ritual blade or *(b)* a staff attuned to a paranormal frequency  
- *(a)* an esoteric grimoire or *(b)* a collection of pre-Emergence texts  
- *(a)* a lightweave cloak or *(b)* an armored shaman’s robe  
- A set of occult tools or paranormal diagnostic instruments  

## **Class Table**  
| Level | Proficiency Bonus | Features |  
|:-:|:-:|:--|  
| 1st | +2 | Spellcasting, Druidic |  
| 2nd | +2 | Shape Reality, Circle of the Veil |  
| 3rd | +2 | - |  
| 4th | +2 | Ability Score Improvement, Minor Reality Shift |  
| 5th | +3 | Paranormal Sense |  
| 6th | +3 | Circle Feature |  
| 7th | +3 | - |  
| 8th | +3 | Ability Score Improvement, Eldritch Resistance |  
| 9th | +4 | Alter Terrain |  
| 10th | +4 | Circle Feature |  
| 11th | +4 | - |  
| 12th | +4 | Ability Score Improvement |  
| 13th | +5 | - |  
| 14th | +5 | Circle Feature |  
| 15th | +5 | - |  
| 16th | +5 | Ability Score Improvement |  
| 17th | +6 | Paranormal Mastery |  
| 18th | +6 | Timeless Body |  
| 19th | +6 | Ability Score Improvement |  
| 20th | +6 | Reality Anchor |  

\page
## **Class Abilities**  
### **Spellcasting (Level 1)**  
You channel **paranormal energy** through rites and rituals. See the Druid spell list for available options.

### **Druidic (Level 1)**  
You know **Druidic**, a secret language spoken only by those who understand the lost whispers of the world.

## **Subclasses**  
At **2nd level**, you choose a Druidic Circle that defines your approach to reality.

### **Shape Reality (Level 2)**  
Instead of traditional Wild Shape, you can subtly **alter the fabric of existence**:  
- Change minor environmental features.  
- Shift the color of an object or minorly distort perception.  
- Sense the **paranormal imprints** left behind by The Emergence.  


## Druid Circles  

---

### **Circle of Rust **  
*"Metal rots like flesh. The city was never built to last."*  

#### **Features & Playstyle**  
- **Manipulates rust, corrosion, and the slow death of infrastructure.**  
- Wields **disease, metal decay, and ruin** to reclaim urban spaces.  
- Common among **urban scavengers, ruin-dwellers, and eco-terrorists.**  

#### **Circle Abilities**  
| Level | Feature |  
|-------|---------|  
| 2nd | **Rust Touch** – You can corrode metal with a touch. As an action, weaken a metallic object, causing it to rust, jam, or break. |  
| 6th | **Decay Spreads** – Your spells ignore resistance to necrotic or poison damage when targeting constructs and inorganic creatures. |  
| 10th | **Steel to Dust** – You can cast *Heat Metal* without concentration, causing severe rusting on metallic surfaces. |  
| 14th | **Urban Collapse** – Once per long rest, you can weaken a **20-foot radius** of concrete, metal, or stone, causing structural collapse. |  

---

### **Circle of Neon**  
*"The lights never go out, and neither do I."*  

#### **Features & Playstyle**  
- **Harnesses city lights, digital signals, and electrical currents.**  
- Merges **druidic power with technology, adapting to the cybernetic city.**  
- Common among **hacked consciousnesses, cyber-druids, and rogue technicians.**  

#### **Circle Abilities**  
| Level | Feature |  
|-------|---------|  
| 2nd | **Neon Veins** – Your spells can be flavored as digital glitches or bursts of static. You can touch a powered device to either short-circuit it or overcharge it. |  
| 6th | **Electric Overdrive** – Gain resistance to lightning damage. Your melee attacks deal extra lightning damage equal to your Wisdom modifier. |  
| 10th | **Citywide Broadcast** – Once per long rest, you can cast *Sending* or *Suggestion* through the city’s wireless networks, targeting any device-connected creature. |  
| 14th | **Become the Signal** – Once per long rest, you can dissolve into pure data, traveling through wires, cameras, or digital screens for up to 1 minute. |  

---

### **Circle of the Hollow**  
*"Some places refuse to be remembered."*  

#### **Features & Playstyle**  
- **Masters of abandoned buildings, forgotten alleyways, and dead spaces.**  
- Uses **urban entropy, liminal spaces, and psychological horror.**  
- Common among **urban shamans, ghost druids, and reality-warped wanderers.**  

#### **Circle Abilities**  
| Level | Feature |  
|-------|---------|  
| 2nd | **Liminal Step** – You can step into an abandoned doorway or alley and emerge from another within 60 feet. |  
| 6th | **Veil of the Forgotten** – While inside an unoccupied building or alleyway, you are invisible to creatures unless they directly interact with you. |  
| 10th | **Echoes of the Past** – You can hear faint, distorted voices and visions of a location’s past when you rest in it. Gain *Legend Lore* once per long rest. |  
| 14th | **Reality Glitch** – Once per long rest, you can distort local reality, causing a **20-foot area** to flicker unpredictably for 1 minute (forcing Wisdom saves or causing creatures to become lost). |  

---

### **Circle of the Vermin**  
*"Nature didn’t leave. It just changed."*  

#### **Features & Playstyle**  
- **Masters of rats, insects, and other urban survivors.**  
- Thrives in **trash, ruins, and abandoned places.**  
- Common among **waste shamans, slum-dwellers, and gutter prophets.**  

\page

#### **Circle Abilities**  
| Level | Feature |  
|-------|---------|  
| 2nd | **Urban Swarm** – Summon a swarm of rats, cockroaches, or pigeons that obey simple commands. They can distract, fetch objects, or harass enemies. |  
| 6th | **Filthborn** – Gain resistance to poison and disease. You can also eat spoiled food without suffering harm. |  
| 10th | **Plague Conduit** – Once per long rest, you can **spread a supernatural sickness**, causing enemies within 15 feet to become poisoned for 1 minute. |  
| 14th | **Swarm Body** – Once per long rest, you can dissolve into a writhing mass of vermin for up to 1 minute, making you immune to non-magical attacks and allowing you to move through cracks and vents. |  

---

### **Circle of Steel**  
*"The world is steel and stone. And I am its guardian."*  

#### **Features & Playstyle**  
- **Masters of industrial landscapes, factories, and reinforced structures.**  
- Wields **metal, machinery, and unbreakable resolve.**  
- Common among **factory workers, urban druids, and self-proclaimed gods of industry.**  

#### **Circle Abilities**  
| Level | Feature |  
|-------|---------|  
| 2nd | **Metal Communion** – Gain proficiency with medium armor and smith’s tools. You can communicate simple thoughts to nearby machinery. |  
| 6th | **Iron Hide** – Gain resistance to non-magical slashing and piercing damage. Your skin hardens, reflecting the resilience of the city itself. |  
| 10th | **Urban Bulwark** – Once per long rest, you can **reinforce a structure**, preventing it from collapsing and increasing its AC and hit points. |  
| 14th | **Titan’s Form** – Once per long rest, you can transform into a **gargantuan construct** for 1 minute, gaining temporary HP and increased strength. |  

---

### **Circle of the Wires**  
*"The trees are gone. But the wires still whisper."*  

#### **Features & Playstyle**  
- **Masters of the city’s hidden networks, radio waves, and data streams.**  
- Uses **digital spirits, machine consciousness, and encrypted magic.**  
- Common among **hacker-druids, ghost coders, and those who speak to the city’s artificial soul.**  

#### **Circle Abilities**  
| Level | Feature |  
|-------|---------|  
| 2nd | **Ghost in the Code** – Gain proficiency in hacking and access to the city’s surveillance feeds for basic data. |  
| 6th | **Electro-Adaptation** – Gain resistance to lightning and immunity to being stunned. Your reaction speed increases, allowing you to act first in initiative once per long rest. |  
| 10th | **Viral Presence** – Once per long rest, you can implant **a hidden message** into a system, forcing machines and devices to relay your words when accessed. |  
| 14th | **Dataform Shift** – Once per long rest, you can temporarily upload yourself into the city’s digital infrastructure, traveling through networks for up to 1 minute. |  


---

### **Circle of the Smog**  
*"Breathe deep. The city is inside you now."*  

#### **Features & Playstyle**  
- **Masters of smoke, pollution, and toxic adaptation.**  
- Spreads **corrosive mists, industrial poisons, and suffocating gases.**  
- Common among **refinery mystics, wasteland wanderers, and poison cultists.**  

#### **Circle Abilities**  
| Level | Feature |  
|-------|---------|  
| 2nd | **Toxic Resilience** – Gain resistance to poison and immunity to airborne toxins. You can survive in low-oxygen environments. |  
| 6th | **Smog Cloud** – You can exhale a 10-foot-radius cloud of toxic gas, lightly obscuring the area and poisoning creatures inside it. |  
| 10th | **Industrial Affliction** – Once per long rest, you can cause a target to start coughing violently, making them unable to cast spells or communicate for 1 minute. |  
| 14th | **Living Pollution** – You can transform into a **being of smog and toxins** for 1 minute, gaining resistance to all damage except force and psychic. |  

---

### **Circle of the Scrapyard**  
*"Nature didn’t die. It just turned into something sharper."*  

#### **Features & Playstyle**  
- **Masters of scavenged magic, repurposed waste, and forgotten relics.**  
- Can **bend metal, animate debris, and create weapons from scrap.**  
- Common among **wasteland druids, urban scavengers, and scrapyard mystics.**  

\page

#### **Circle Abilities**  
| Level | Feature |  
|-------|---------|  
| 2nd | **Junk Mage** – You can use pieces of scrap metal and discarded objects as druidic focuses for spellcasting. |  
| 6th | **Scrap Armor** – Gain +1 AC while wearing light or medium armor. You can create makeshift armor from debris in 1 hour. |  
| 10th | **Animate Debris** – Once per long rest, you can bring a pile of trash or scrap to life, acting as a temporary construct under your control for 1 minute. |  
| 14th | **Scrap Titan** – You can shape-shift into a **golem of industrial waste**, gaining temporary HP and increased melee damage. |  

---

### **Circle of the Forgotten**  
*"The past never leaves. It just waits to be heard."*  

#### **Features & Playstyle**  
- **Channels the memories of forgotten places and urban decay.**  
- Uses **hauntings, echoes, and residual emotions** as power.  
- Common among **spirit mediums, urban shamans, and keepers of lost knowledge.**  

#### **Circle Abilities**  
| Level | Feature |  
|-------|---------|  
| 2nd | **Echo Sense** – When entering an abandoned place, you can see brief flashes of its past occupants. |  
| 6th | **Whispers of the Ruins** – Gain advantage on Investigation and Perception checks in places that haven’t been inhabited in at least a year. |  
| 10th | **Lingering Spirits** – Once per long rest, you can call forth a ghostly presence that answers one question truthfully. |  
| 14th | **Reawaken the Lost** – Once per long rest, you can restore a destroyed location or object to a past version of itself for 24 hours. |  

---

### **Circle of the Railways**  
*"Steel veins pump the lifeblood of the city. Ride the current."*  

#### **Features & Playstyle**  
- **Masters of movement, transit, and high-speed travel.**  
- Gains **unnatural speed, terrain adaptation, and teleportation abilities.**  
- Common among **train cultists, subway shamans, and speed demons.**  

#### **Circle Abilities**  
| Level | Feature |  
|-------|---------|  
| 2nd | **Urban Stride** – You ignore difficult terrain in cities and can move through narrow spaces without squeezing. |  
| 6th | **Railrunner’s Rush** – Your movement speed increases by 10 feet. You can use a reaction to move 10 feet when an enemy misses you. |  
| 10th | **Ghost Train Step** – Once per long rest, you can teleport up to 60 feet as long as you start and end your movement on a road, track, or transit line. |  
| 14th | **Speed of the City** – While in urban environments, you can take the Dash action as a bonus action. |  

---

### **Circle of Concrete**  
*"Nature has not died. It has evolved into something stronger."*  

#### **Features & Playstyle**  
- **Masters of concrete, asphalt, and city-built landscapes.**  
- Gains abilities tied to **walls, structural reinforcement, and urban control.**  
- Common among **brutalist monks, urban guardians, and concrete-bound sages.**  

#### **Circle Abilities**  
| Level | Feature |  
|-------|---------|  
| 2nd | **Concrete Communion** – Gain proficiency with Mason’s tools. You can sense weak points in buildings and structures. |  
| 6th | **Hardened Skin** – While standing on artificial surfaces, you gain +1 AC and resistance to non-magical damage. |  
| 10th | **City’s Grip** – You can meld into a concrete wall for up to 1 minute, becoming undetectable while inside. |  
| 14th | **The City Endures** – Once per long rest, you can reinforce an entire structure within 100 feet, preventing it from collapsing or being destroyed for 24 hours. |  

---

### **Circle of the Echo Grid**  
*"The city hums. I know how to listen."*  

#### **Features & Playstyle**  
- **Wields sound waves, vibrations, and city noise as power.**  
- Uses **resonance, subsonic influence, and auditory disruption.**  
- Common among **urban mystics, sound engineers, and acoustic shamans.**  

\page

#### **Circle Abilities**  
| Level | Feature |  
|-------|---------|  
| 2nd | **Echo Tuning** – Gain proficiency in Performance. You can manipulate echoes to mimic voices or mask sounds. |  
| 6th | **Sonic Resilience** – Gain resistance to thunder damage. You cannot be deafened. |  
| 10th | **Disrupting Frequencies** – Once per long rest, you can create a **30-foot field of distorted sound**, imposing disadvantage on spellcasting that requires verbal components. |  
| 14th | **Resonant Collapse** – Once per long rest, you can shatter glass, metal, and unstable structures within a **30-foot radius**, forcing creatures to make a Strength saving throw or be knocked prone. |  

---

## **Multiclassing**  
If your campaign allows multiclassing, use the following rules for a **Druid** multiclass character.  

### **Ability Score Minimums**  
- Wisdom 13  

### **Proficiencies Gained**  
- Light armor, medium armor, shields (no metal)  

---

## **Quick Build**  
You can make a **Druid** quickly by following these suggestions:  
- Choose **Elf or Tiefling** for a thematic fit.  
- Pick the **Occultist** or **Hermit** background.  
- Prioritize **Wisdom**, followed by **Intelligence**.  
- Take a ritual blade and an esoteric grimoire for roleplay potential.
