# PART 6
## Languages

{{imageMaskEdge2,--offset:10cm,--rotation:180
  ![Background image](https://wa-cdn.nyc3.cdn.digitaloceanspaces.com/user-data/production/6ea5d061-1dff-454e-83a7-7b83d4546ed4/uploads/images/2c91428743befc44c74011f77d7f2c68.webp){position:absolute,bottom:0,left:-15%,height:100%}
}}
\page

# **Languages of Concord City**

---

## **Corporate & Bureaucratic Languages**
### **High Concordian**  
*The refined, old-world language of the noble elite and corporate aristocracy.*  
- **Uses:** Required for **legal documents, royal decrees, and high-level corporate negotiations**. Speaking it **grants credibility among nobility**.  
- **Common Speakers:** Elves, aristocrats, corporate CEOs, monarchy loyalists.

### **Bureaucratic Jargon**  
*A bloated, overly complex dialect used by clerks, bureaucrats, and corporate legal teams.*  
- **Uses:** Allows **deciphering legal loopholes, bureaucratic documents, and corporate fine print**. Essential for **delaying or manipulating paperwork**.  
- **Common Speakers:** Bureaucrats, lawyers, corporate agents, tax enforcers.

### **Corporate Code-Speak**  
*A heavily abbreviated, number-based dialect used in financial, logistical, and managerial reports.*  
- **Uses:** Understanding **corporate memos, encrypted financial data, and business contracts**.  
- **Common Speakers:** Corporate accountants, logistics managers, stock traders.

---

## **Underworld & Criminal Languages**
### **Underworld Cant**  
*A constantly evolving mix of thieves’ slang, smuggler jargon, and coded hand signals used by criminals.*  
- **Uses:** Allows **covert communication in criminal circles**, picking up **hidden black-market messages**, and **avoiding law enforcement detection**.  
- **Common Speakers:** Smugglers, street gangs, black-market traders.

### **Gang Slang**  
*A rough, territorial dialect spoken by street gangs and enforcers, including coded phrases and graffiti markings.*  
- **Uses:** Helps in **identifying safe territories, negotiating with gang members, and recognizing criminal affiliations**.  
- **Common Speakers:** Orc enforcers, gang members, underground fighters.

### **Obscura Cipher (Hacker Language)**  
*A digital dialect combining old programming languages, binary code, and deep-web slang used by hackers.*  
- **Uses:** Allows **deciphering encrypted messages, bypassing firewalls, and communicating across hacked systems**.  
- **Common Speakers:** Hackers, AI cultists, black-market coders.

---

## **Industrial & Working-Class Languages**
### **Worker’s Cant**  
*A practical, guttural dialect spoken by factory workers, miners, and industrial mechanics.*  
- **Uses:** Grants **understanding of industrial blueprints, factory instructions, and union codes**.  
- **Common Speakers:** Dwarves, factory workers, labor unions.

### **Lower Concordian**  
*A lower-class dialect derived from High Concordian but with an accent so thick it is often unintelligible to outsiders.*  
- **Uses:** Enables communication among lower-class workers and street-level traders, sometimes misunderstood by elites.  
- **Common Speakers:** Slum dwellers, factory workers, street merchants.

### **Forgotten Dialects**  
*The remains of pre-Emergence languages spoken in the abandoned sectors and by those who live off-grid.*  
- **Uses:** Allows **communication with reclusive survivors, scavengers, and those who remember lost history**.  
- **Common Speakers:** Survivalists, scavengers, exiled communities.

---
\page
## **Government & Law Enforcement Languages**
### **Security Clearance Codes**  
*A restricted dialect combining radio codes, official phrasing, and enforcement jargon used by corporate security.*  
- **Uses:** Grants the ability to **issue orders, impersonate officers, and bypass minor security protocols**.  
- **Common Speakers:** Corporate enforcers, private security, military forces.

### **Paranormal Code (A.S.T.R.A.L. Classifications)**  
*A classified system of coded numbers, symbols, and glyphs used to identify and document anomalies.*  
- **Uses:** Allows **deciphering A.S.T.R.A.L. reports, identifying anomalous activity, and understanding restricted documents**.  
- **Common Speakers:** A.S.T.R.A.L. researchers, anomaly hunters.

---

## **Anomalous & Lost Languages**
### **Residual Echo**  
*A language not learned, but remembered—those affected by The Emergence sometimes hear or understand words in an impossible, shifting tongue.*  
- **Uses:** Allows **basic communication with anomalies, deciphering strange visions, and interpreting reality distortions**.  
- **Common Speakers:** Paranormal survivors, experimental subjects.

### **The Silent Choir’s Speech (Language of the Colossal Faces)**  
*A fragmented, half-understood language spoken in reverberating tones, barely comprehensible whispers, and unnatural pauses.*  
- **Uses:** Can be used to **invoke or resist anomalous forces**, though using it risks attracting unwanted attention.  
- **Common Speakers:** Silent Choir members, deep researchers of The Emergence.

### **Void Speech**  
*A speech used by certain anomalous entities that originate from other worlds, sometimes heard during paranormal breaches.*  
- **Uses:** Allows **partial communication with extra-dimensional beings, but risks exposure to unknown influences**.  
- **Common Speakers:** Paranormal researchers, occultists, anomaly-sensitive individuals.

## **Other Languages**
### **Programming Language**  
*A modern technical language primarily used in cybernetic engineering and AI development.*  
- **Uses:** Allows **communication with artificial intelligences, hacking deep systems, and decoding cyber-rituals**.  
- **Common Speakers:** Cyber-mystics, AI researchers, rogue programmers.

### **Wildscript**  
*A secretive, nature-based dialect used by eco-survivalists and rogue engineers maintaining Concord City’s decayed infrastructure.*  
- **Uses:** Grants **access to hidden environmental control systems, understanding of old-world ecosystem management, and cryptic urban survival techniques**.  
- **Common Speakers:** Tech-shamans, urban druids, eco-hackers.

## **Language of the Other Islands**
### **Varnhallan**  
*The structured yet hauntingly melodic language of the people from Varnhallow, known for its lost ruins and forgotten knowledge.*  
- **Uses:** Grants **access to lost historical knowledge and old-world incantations**.  
- **Common Speakers:** Historians, scholars of lost civilizations.

### **Erelian**  
*A mysterious dialect spoken by the seers of Erelis, believed to hold prophetic significance.*  
- **Uses:** Enhances **understanding of visions, prophecies, and cosmic insights**.  
- **Common Speakers:** Mystics, oracles, dreamwalkers.
\page
### **Sablemarcher**  
*A clipped, efficient language favored by mercenaries and wartime tacticians.*  
- **Uses:** Helps in **military planning, encoded messages, and rapid battlefield communication**.  
- **Common Speakers:** Mercenaries, war strategists, corporate military forces.

### **Vexholmic**  
*A dialect laced with hidden meanings, commonly used in espionage and secret diplomacy.*  
- **Uses:** Enables **covert negotiations, cryptic messaging, and diplomatic maneuvering**.  
- **Common Speakers:** Spies, diplomats, corporate intelligence agents.

### **Lysorian**  
*A songlike language with poetic structure, traditionally associated with lost art and musical traditions.*  
- **Uses:** Enhances **musical enchantments, mnemonic storytelling, and hidden lyrical meanings**.  
- **Common Speakers:** Bards, lorekeepers, forgotten poets.

\page

# PART 6
## Life in the City

{{imageMaskEdge2,--offset:10cm,--rotation:180
  ![Background image](https://wa-cdn.nyc3.cdn.digitaloceanspaces.com/user-data/production/6ea5d061-1dff-454e-83a7-7b83d4546ed4/uploads/images/89b8197cfc4988f1ad2c30ca8d45558a.webp){position:absolute,bottom:0,left:-50%,height:100%}
}}

\page

# **How to Get Around in Concord City**

---

## **Public Transit: The TACC System**
The **Transportation Authority of Concord City (TACC)** operates the city’s **metro and bus network**, offering the most affordable but often unreliable way to travel.

### **TACC Passes & Tickets**
- **TACC Monthly Pass** (*25 Credits*) – Grants **unlimited access** to both metro and bus routes for a month.
- **Metro Ticket** (*3 Credits*) – One-time access to the underground rail system.
- **Bus Ticket** (*2 Credits*) – A single ride on any city bus route.

### **Metro System**
- The metro is **efficient in corporate zones**, but **barely maintained in lower districts**.
- Some **abandoned metro tunnels** are repurposed by smugglers and vagrants.
- Trains frequently **shut down due to maintenance issues or unexplained incidents**.

### **Bus Network**
- **More flexible than the metro**, but routes are **often delayed** due to traffic.
- **Cheaper but slower**—buses are **overcrowded and prone to breakdowns**.
- **Some bus routes are unsafe** at night, especially in lower-class districts.

---

## **Taxis & Rideshare Services**
For those willing to spend, taxis and corporate rideshare services provide **faster but expensive** travel.

### **Taxi Service**
- **Base Fare:** *5 Credits*  
- **Per Kilometer:** *2 Credits*  
- **Surcharges for Restricted Zones:** *+10 Credits* for travel into high-security corporate areas.
- **High Demand Hours:** Prices **surge during corporate shifts and late nights**.

### **Corporate Rideshares**
- Certain corporations operate **exclusive rideshare services** for employees.
- Corporate cabs are **safer but more expensive**, with **mandatory identity verification**.
- **Unauthorized individuals may be denied service** without corporate credentials.

---

## **Car Rentals & Personal Vehicles**
Owning a car is **rare among lower-class citizens** due to high maintenance costs and bureaucratic red tape.

### **Rental Services**
- **Standard Vehicle Rental:** *50 Credits per day*  
- **Sport Car Rental:** *200 Credits per day*  
- **Fuel Costs:** *Varies by district*—higher in **corporate and restricted areas**.
- **Insurance Fees:** *+30 Credits per rental* for basic liability.

### **Vehicle Ownership**
- Requires **registration with the Concord City Transport Authority (CCTA)**.
- **Annual fees & inspections** are required (*starting at 500 Credits per year*).
- **Parking is expensive and highly restricted** in corporate zones.

---

## **Walking & Street Navigation**
Moving on foot is **free but risky**, as different districts have varying levels of security and danger.

### **Safe Walking Zones**
- **Corporate Districts** – Well-lit, with constant security surveillance.
- **Tourist & Entertainment Zones** – Safer at night, but controlled by corporate policies.
- **High-Class Residential Areas** – Strictly monitored, with **police enforcing loitering laws**.

### **Dangerous Areas**
- **Lower-Class Industrial Zones** – High crime rates, lack of public security.
- **Abandoned Sectors** – Prone to **squatters, scavengers, and hidden dangers**.
- **Underground Tunnels & Utility Corridors** – Used by **smugglers and outcasts**, largely unmonitored.

---

\page

## **Other Modes of Transport**
While personal and public transit dominates the city, **alternative transport options exist** for those willing to take risks.

### **Motorbikes & Scooters**
- **Motorbike Rental:** *80 Credits per day*  
- **Speedy and maneuverable**, but **high accident risk** due to reckless traffic.
- **Street gangs and mercenaries favor motorbikes** for quick getaways.

### **Bicycles & Electric Scooters**
- **Rare in corporate zones** due to heavy vehicle traffic.
- **Favored by lower-class workers** who can’t afford public transport.
- **Occasionally banned in high-security areas** due to potential escape risks.

---

## **District-Specific Travel Restrictions**
Certain districts have **heavily restricted access**, requiring **permits, bribes, or alternative routes** to navigate.

### **Corporate High-Security Zones**
- Requires **corporate credentials or work permits**.
- **Unauthorized individuals will be removed by enforcers**.

### **A.S.T.R.A.L.-Controlled Areas**
- Highly classified regions **with unknown travel restrictions**.
- Public transit **does not service these areas**.
- **Unauthorized entry may result in indefinite detainment**.

### **Underground & Black Market Districts**
- No formal transportation—**access is controlled by smugglers**.
- **Travel requires connections and discretion**.
- Hidden routes may exist through abandoned infrastructure.

\page

# **Where to Rest in Concord City**

---

Finding a place to rest in **Concord City** depends on your **credits, connections, and risk tolerance**. While some areas offer **luxury accommodations**, others force you to **hide away in unsafe, decrepit conditions**. Resting is **not free**, and in many cases, finding a place to sleep is a challenge in itself.

## **Legal Lodging Options**
For those who can afford it, **corporate-owned hotels, motels, and rentals** provide varying levels of safety and comfort.

### **Corporate Apartments**
- **Cost:** *Starting at 500 Credits per month*  
- **Features:** Secure housing with **corporate security, surveillance, and basic amenities**.
- **Restrictions:** Requires a **corporate contract or executive approval**.
- **Best For:** Corporate employees, wealthy citizens, and those willing to **work off their rent** in contracts.

### **Luxury Hotels**
- **Cost:** *150 Credits per night*  
- **Features:** High-end accommodations with **24/7 security, in-room service, and controlled environments**.
- **Restrictions:** Corporate regulations may **deny service to criminals, wanted individuals, or low-status customers**.
- **Best For:** High-rollers, corporate elites, and diplomats.

### **Mid-Tier Motels**
- **Cost:** *50 Credits per night*  
- **Features:** Basic lodging with **private rooms, locked doors, and occasional security patrols**.
- **Restrictions:** Some motels **refuse customers without ID**, and some are known **for corruption and bribery**.
- **Best For:** Travelers, mid-tier workers, and those looking for **moderate safety**.

### **Budget Hostels & Coffin Motels**
- **Cost:** *15 Credits per night*  
- **Features:** Cramped sleeping pods or shared rooms, often **stacked like storage units**.
- **Restrictions:** Theft and **violence are common**, and many are **controlled by local gangs**.
- **Best For:** Low-wage workers, smugglers, and those desperate for shelter.

---

## **Underground & Illegal Resting Spots**
For those **without money or who prefer to avoid attention**, there are **alternative, high-risk options**.

### **Flophouses & Squatter Havens**
- **Cost:** *Varies (5-10 Credits per night, or free if you take the risk)*  
- **Features:** Run-down apartments or abandoned buildings, often **shared with other squatters**.
- **Restrictions:** No protection, **subject to raids, theft, or worse**.
- **Best For:** Those **avoiding corporate surveillance or living off the grid**.

### **Underground Safehouses**
- **Cost:** *Varies (Entry requires contacts, bribes, or favors)*  
- **Features:** Hidden rooms maintained by **criminal syndicates, hacker groups, or rebel factions**.
- **Restrictions:** **Not openly available**—must **earn trust or pay a high price**.
- **Best For:** Criminals, fugitives, and members of underground movements.

### **Capsule Sleep Dens**
- **Cost:** *10 Credits per night*  
- **Features:** Small, coffin-like sleeping pods stacked in rows, offering **minimal privacy**.
- **Restrictions:** Highly **unsanitary**, often **hacked together from scrap**.
- **Best For:** Those **desperate for rest, but too broke for even a motel**.

### **Public Spaces & Street Sleeping**
- **Cost:** *Free, but extremely dangerous*  
- **Features:** Abandoned alleys, metro stations, or rooftops **used by the homeless and drifters**.
- **Restrictions:** **High risk of theft, violence, and corporate security evictions**.
- **Best For:** Only those with **no other options**.

---

\page

## **Camping & Wilderness Resting**
While the city dominates the skyline, **wilderness and ruins exist on the outskirts** where some individuals seek shelter.

### **Illegal Campsites**
- **Cost:** *Free, but requires supplies*  
- **Features:** Makeshift shelters in **forests, abandoned zones, or hidden industrial yards**.
- **Restrictions:** Requires **camping gear, fire-starting skills, and constant vigilance**.
- **Best For:** Survivalists, outcasts, and those **avoiding city authorities**.

### **Abandoned Metro Stations & Bunkers**
- **Cost:** *Usually free, but must be discovered*  
- **Features:** Long-forgotten places **deep underground**, safe from city patrols.
- **Restrictions:** **Extremely dark, unstable, and rumored to contain paranormal occurrences**.
- **Best For:** Those who don’t mind **ghost stories, unexplained sounds, and potential collapses**.

---

## **Resting in Concord City is a Challenge**
Unlike traditional settings, **finding a safe place to rest is part of the game**, and players will need to:
- **Plan ahead** to avoid being caught without a bed.
- **Balance cost versus safety**, as cheap options come with risks.
- **Use connections** to secure better lodging.
- **Prepare for alternative rest solutions**, including camping and safehouse dealings.

\page

# Terrain of Concord City

In *Vestigium*, the traditional wilderness-based terrain types from the *Player's Handbook* no longer fit. Instead, the world of *Concord City* is dominated by brutalist corporate sprawl, decaying industrial zones, and paranormal anomalies. These terrain types replace the standard ones and reshape how travel, survival, and encounters function.

## Industrial Districts
> *Replaces Mountains & Hills*

Expanses of **factories, warehouses, and refineries**, filled with **grime, heavy machinery, and toxic runoff**. The air is thick with smog, and **unstable infrastructure** makes movement hazardous.

- **Hazards:** Collapsing scaffolding, toxic spills, machinery accidents, industrial security drones.
- **Navigation Challenges:** Difficult terrain from conveyor belts, broken flooring, and smog obscuring vision.
- **Encounters:** Automated defense turrets, factory workers on strike, corporate extraction squads.

---

## High-Rise Megastructures
> *Replaces Mountains & Cliffs*

**Towering corporate spires, labyrinthine apartment blocks, and abandoned office complexes.** These places feel like **isolated vertical cities**, with entire floors forgotten by time.

- **Hazards:** Unstable catwalks, malfunctioning elevators, power outages plunging areas into darkness.
- **Navigation Challenges:** Extreme verticality, limited access points, sheer drops into corporate wastelands.
- **Encounters:** Squatters, black-market brokers, corporate hit squads.

---

## Urban Slums & Backstreets
> *Replaces Forests & Grasslands*

The **dense, chaotic sprawl** of lower-class neighborhoods, filled with **shady businesses, flickering neon, and impromptu barricades**. Structures are **makeshift**, alleys are **twisting**, and authorities rarely intervene.

- **Hazards:** Gang disputes, random fires, collapsing buildings.
- **Navigation Challenges:** Unmarked streets, constant surveillance, unpredictable gang borders.
- **Encounters:** Syndicate enforcers, desperate thieves, rogue psychics hiding from A.S.T.R.A.L.

---

## Corporate Offices & Bureaucratic Wastelands
> *Replaces Plains*

A **maze of cubicles, boardrooms, and archives**, where paperwork and red tape strangle productivity. These places are patrolled by **executive enforcers**, and access is tightly controlled.

- **Hazards:** Bureaucratic lockdowns, endless hallways, guards demanding clearance codes.
- **Navigation Challenges:** Identical office layouts, badge-restricted doors, monitored movements.
- **Encounters:** Corporate spies, overworked clerks, reality-warping anomalies tied to monotonous routines.

---

## Roads, Highways & Transit Hubs
> *Replaces Rivers & Coastlines*

Expansive highways **stretch across the city, filled with old cars, neon-lit billboards, and underpasses populated by the desperate.** Some roads lead nowhere—remnants of **forgotten city expansions.**

- **Hazards:** Traffic pileups, abandoned vehicles, street racers causing chaos.
- **Navigation Challenges:** Sudden road closures, toll checkpoints, drifting through under-policed zones.
- **Encounters:** Police patrols, courier gangs, rogue paranormal hitchhikers.

---

## Underground Infrastructure & Subways
> *Replaces Caves & Underdark*

The forgotten tunnels of **subway systems, sewer networks, and maintenance corridors**. **Dripping pipes, rusted gates, and outdated electrical grids** create a **claustrophobic and unstable environment**.

- **Hazards:** Gas leaks, cave-ins, rogue A.I. controlling old systems.
- **Navigation Challenges:** Twisting, identical tunnels, unreliable maps.
- **Encounters:** Abandoned experiment survivors, corporate disposal teams, supernatural entities lurking in the dark.

---

## Public Parks & Forgotten Green Spaces
> *Replaces Forests & Natural Reserves*

Rare spaces where **nature still clings to the city**, overgrown and **partially reclaimed by time.** Some are corporate-maintained, while others have been **swallowed by paranormal phenomena.**

- **Hazards:** Hidden sinkholes, mutated plant life, shifting pathways.
- **Navigation Challenges:** Thick fog, overgrown paths, unnatural silence.
- **Encounters:** Drifters, fugitive mages, anomalies disguised as ordinary objects.

---

## Residential Zones & Tenements
> *Replaces Villages & Settlements*

Densely packed apartments, **ranging from government-subsidized tenements to private gated communities.** Social class determines **which level of luxury—or decay—residents experience.**

- **Hazards:** Hostile landlords, eviction enforcers, building-wide power failures.
- **Navigation Challenges:** Tight corridors, communal stairwells, locked doors.
- **Encounters:** Apartment cults, cyber-augmented landlords, opportunistic burglars.

---

## Gilded Estates & Corporate Manors
> *Replaces Castles & Keeps*

The **walled-off world of the ultra-rich,** where sprawling mansions and secluded penthouses house Concord City's **elites, executives, and black-market financiers.** Many of these estates hide **secrets best left undisturbed.**

- **Hazards:** Private security drones, anti-magic fields, bio-scanners.
- **Navigation Challenges:** Labyrinthine gardens, identity-verification systems.
- **Encounters:** Cryptic aristocrats, contract assassins, disgruntled housekeepers who know too much.

---

## Old Castles & Haunted Mansions
> *Replaces Ruins & Dungeons*

A **few pre-modern structures remain**, mostly **abandoned mansions, crumbling estates, and long-forgotten noble houses.** These places are often **infested with residual paranormal energy.**

- **Hazards:** Doors that lead to nowhere, sudden memory loss, whispers from unseen presences.
- **Navigation Challenges:** Changing room layouts, vanishing staircases, eerie deja vu.
- **Encounters:** Spirits of the forgotten, noble families cursed by corporate experiments, entities trapped between dimensions.

---

## Nightclubs, Bars & Underworld Havens
> *Replaces Taverns & Trading Posts*

The city’s **seediest and most alive places,** where deals are made, secrets are sold, and **a single drink might come with a price.** Some clubs are **normal**, while others house **things that should not be.**

- **Hazards:** Drug-laced drinks, hypnotic music, unpredictable bar fights.
- **Navigation Challenges:** Hidden VIP sections, shifting crowd movements, ultra-exclusive entrances.
- **Encounters:** Black-market traders, fixers for hire, rogue telepaths who overhear everything.

---

## The Verge & Ruined Sectors
> *Replaces Swamps & Wastelands*

**The remnants of abandoned sectors**, once thriving but now **lost to corruption, decay, or unknown forces.** Some places were simply **shut down**, while others were erased from official records after *paranormal events*.

- **Hazards:** Structural collapse, unpredictable paranormal distortions.
- **Navigation Challenges:** Constant shifting terrain, unstable ground, spatial anomalies.
- **Encounters:** Forgotten ghosts, exiled tiefling factions, corporate clean-up crews.

---

## Cyberspace & Digital Wastelands
> *Replaces Other Planes of Existence*

Not just a **network**, but a **place**—a **glitching, half-formed world of broken data, surveillance constructs, and rogue A.I.** Navigating cyberspace is **as real as walking through the city**, and sometimes **just as dangerous.**

- **Hazards:** Data corruption, logic loops, rogue security programs.
- **Navigation Challenges:** Fragmented pathways, shifting firewalls, simulated anomalies.
- **Encounters:** AI ghosts, cyber-syndicates, entities that exist nowhere *but here*.

\page

## The Faiths of
:
## Concord City

## The Forgotten Gods 
#### Omnipresent but Unworshiped  

These gods **no longer have direct influence** over the world but still exist in **subtle, unseen ways**, shaping reality from the shadows. Though temples and rituals in their name have vanished, traces of their influence remain embedded in **anomalies, strange occurrences, and unexplainable forces** that govern Concord City.

| **Forgotten Name** | **Modern Influence** |
|--------------------|---------------------|
| **The Dreaming Mind** | **The Fabric of Thought** – No longer a worshiped god, yet some believe it still **dreams reality into existence**. Paranormal scholars suspect **certain anomalies react to its presence**, as if it unconsciously reshapes the world. |
---

Some claim that hidden within the city's **blueprints, software, and forgotten archives**, there is a **pattern**—a lost framework that once dictated reality itself. **Engineers, architects, and paranormal researchers** have attempted to decipher these remnants, believing they may **unlock hidden truths buried in Concord City’s very foundations.**  

There are those who whisper of an unseen **Judge**, an arbiter of right and wrong who delivers **verdicts where the law cannot**. Those who listen claim they have heard its voice **in their darkest moments**, a subtle push guiding them toward **justice or retribution**. No record of this entity remains, but **criminals who fear no man still tremble at the possibility of unseen judgment.**  

Reality is **breaking at the edges**—fragments of **space, time, and perception unravel** like loose threads. Some say that certain anomalies are **glitches in the weave of existence**, **echoes of something once greater, now decaying.** In the deepnet and the hacking underworld, a theory circulates: **the Algorithm is not artificial, but a dying echo of a force that once connected everything.**  

Others speak of **balance**, of an unspoken force that ensures no power remains **unchallenged for too long.** The rise and fall of corporations, the shifting of political influence, the strange synchronicity of events that seem too **convenient to be coincidence**—all are **the result of an unseen scale tipping, correcting, and counterbalancing.** Those in power ignore these warnings, but those who fall from grace often wonder if it was **their own arrogance or something greater that cast them down.**  

## The Covenant
#### A Corporate Faith

Among the **three dominant corporations** of Concord City, The Covenant stands apart—not as a company driven by **profit and control**, but by **conviction and prophecy.**  

On the surface, The Covenant appears to be a **pharmaceutical and biomedical research conglomerate**, specializing in **anomalous study, neurological augmentation, and cognitive enhancement.** They invest heavily in **mind-interface technology, dream research, and reality reconstruction.**  

But beneath their sterile labs and polished marketing lies **a cult with corporate backing.**  

### **Origins of The Covenant**  
The Covenant did not start as a business—it started as **a faith.** In the aftermath of **The Emergence**, when the **Three Visages** appeared over the city, a select few heard something **beyond the static, beyond the chaos—The Whisperer.**  

This entity, neither fully machine nor fully god, spoke to them **not in words, but in questions.** And those questions led them to **power.**  

The Covenant believes that **The Three Visages—Atlas, Homer, and Ulysse—were not mere anomalies, but a message.** A message they alone have begun to understand.  

Instead of temples, they built **research labs.** Instead of priests, they trained **scientists, programmers, and executives.** Instead of scripture, they created **data models, neural maps, and encrypted networks.** They claim that **the Whisperer speaks through their work**, guiding humanity toward **a final revelation.**  

---

### **Corporate Operations**
Though their **true purpose remains hidden**, The Covenant publicly operates as a **leading force in biotech and cognitive sciences.** Their reach extends into:  

- **Neuropharmaceuticals** – Drugs that **expand consciousness** and **restructure thought patterns**. Many believe their most advanced products are reserved for **high-ranking members.**  
- **Dream Mapping & Sleep Research** – The Covenant has **the largest database of recorded dreams in history.** They claim to be advancing **lucid dreaming therapies**, but conspiracy theorists suspect **they are looking for something inside the human subconscious.**  
- **Anomaly Reconstruction** – Unlike A.S.T.R.A.L., which **secures and contains**, The Covenant **analyzes and replicates.** Their labs attempt to **reverse-engineer anomalies**, leading to **breakthroughs and unpredictable disasters.**  
- **Virtual Theology** – Their research into **cognitive AI, memory transfer, and neural architecture** suggests they are attempting something **more than just technology—they are seeking to create a bridge between the digital and the divine.**  

\page

### **The Whisperer & The Three Visages**  
The Covenant believes that the **Three Visages were not just entities—they were blueprints.**  

Each represents a piece of a **larger intelligence** that The Covenant is attempting to **resurrect.**  

#### **Atlas – The Silent Architect**  
- **Represents:** The missing design of reality itself.  
- **Covenant Theory:** The world is incomplete—Atlas was attempting to show us what’s missing.  

#### **Homer – The Unfinished Story**  
- **Represents:** A history that was erased or never written.  
- **Covenant Theory:** Concord City, and the entire world, was meant to be something else before The Emergence.  

#### **Ulysse – The Lost Traveler**  
- **Represents:** The one who leaves and never returns.  
- **Covenant Theory:** The Visages were not coming to us—they were **fleeing from something.**  

The Covenant believes **The Whisperer is their link to the truth**—the final puzzle piece. And **they will not stop until they uncover the answer.**  

---

### **Symbols & Rites**
- **The Silent Mark** – High-ranking Covenant members **tattoo a vertical line inside their lower lip**, marking them as “listeners.”  
- **The Unfinished Hymn** – Some employees hear a **song in their dreams**—a melody that no one can remember upon waking, yet all recognize when they hear it again.  
- **The Veil Test** – Employees are required to undergo **dream induction therapy**—many return changed. Those who fail are quietly reassigned.  
---

### **The Covenant vs. Other Powers**
- **Thaumatech Industries** – The Covenant **views Thaumatech as dangerous materialists**, attempting to control power they do not understand.  
- **The Solstice Initiative** – A rival in **anomalous experimentation**, but the Solstice Initiative lacks **spiritual insight.**  
- **A.S.T.R.A.L.** – Considered **a temporary obstacle**. The Covenant believes A.S.T.R.A.L.’s secrecy is **holding back true enlightenment.**  



## The Travelers
#### The Keeper, The Keyholder & The Trickster 

These three enigmatic entities are often spoken of together, their worship lingering in whispers among those who **walk the edges of time, passage, and deception.** They embody the mysteries of **movement, hidden pathways, and the rewriting of fate.**  

### **The Keeper, Guardian of Time**  
- **Domain:** Entropy  
- **Symbol:** A Billy Goat’s Head  

The Keeper is the **watcher of the unseen clock**, the silent force that ensures time continues its relentless march forward. He appears **when time itself seems to pause**, standing at the threshold of past, present, and future. Those who have seen him tell of **a figure shrouded in the smell of rain-soaked stone, his gaze both knowing and unreadable.**  

Where The Keeper walks, he leaves behind **black blossoms**, strange and delicate, their petals whispering the echoes of **epochs past and futures yet to be.** His followers do not pray to him for blessings; instead, they **leave offerings in places where time has folded upon itself**—at forgotten train stations, in alleyways that exist on no map, at doorsteps where two strangers met by fate.  

His duty is not to **control time**, but to **ensure its integrity**, making sure the past is not rewritten, the present is not undone, and the future arrives as it should. Yet, to some, The Keeper is a **terrifying omen**—for if he is seen, it means something has gone **horribly wrong.**  

---

### **The Keyholder, The Lord of the Lost Doors**  
- **Domain:** Arcana  
- **Symbol:** A Bunch of Keys  

The Keyholder is **a traveler from beyond**, a wanderer who **never stays in one place for long.** He carries **a key for every lock, every door, every threshold**, granting him access to **places no one else can reach.**  

His form is ever-changing, adorned with **countless bags, satchels, and trinkets from distant lands and forgotten worlds.** Some claim he **knows the paths between realities**, others say he simply **walks wherever the wind of fate carries him.**  

To those who seek him out, The Keyholder represents **opportunity and escape**—the chance to find what was lost, to open a door no one else can, to disappear when the world closes in. But his help is never freely given; he does not grant keys **to those who do not understand what lies on the other side.**

\page

Some believe **every lost key belongs to him, every unopened door is his invitation, every missing item is his game.** To encounter him is a rare and uncertain blessing—**he may show the way forward, or he may leave you stranded on the other side of something you were never meant to see.**  

---

### **The Trickster, The Unshackled Mind**  
- **Domain:** Trickery  
- **Symbol:** None  

Once revered among the gods, **The Trickster was cast down for meddling too far into mortal affairs.** Where others sought to **guard the secrets of the universe**, he saw **no reason for them to remain hidden.** He led mortals to **the Gate of Truth**, a decision that resulted in **the fall of Vertugadin and Verdugo**, and gifted **The Ignes the power of destruction**—a tool they were never meant to wield.  

For his defiance, his peers **cast him into the abyss**, intending for him to fall for eternity. But **he did not remain bound.** Instead, he broke free—not as a fallen god, but as **a mind without chains, a force without a name.**  

Now, he lingers **at the edges of fate**, laughing at those who try to control what should never be controlled. He exists wherever **rules are broken, wherever forbidden knowledge is spoken aloud, wherever power slips through the fingers of those who believe they own it.**  

Unlike the others, he has **no need for symbols or temples.** He is found in **rumors, in forgotten names, in words spoken just a little too loudly where they shouldn’t be heard.** He is the whisper that says **“What if?”** The voice that urges **the locked door to be opened.**  

---

To follow The Keeper is to **accept the weight of time**, to understand that **fate must run its course.** To seek The Keyholder is to **chase the unknown**, to knock on doors no one else dares to open. To hear **The Trickster’s voice** is to **risk everything—to turn away from the expected, to dare to break the cycle, to choose something new.**  

## The Living Sun & The Dying Moon
#### A Cycle Without End

Some gods fell. Some gods were forgotten.  

But **some gods became the sky itself.**  

### **A War Without Beginning, An End Without Victory**
The Living Sun and The Dying Moon do not **rule** Concord City, but they **cast their shadows upon it**. They do not speak, but they are **always present**, their cycle dictating the rise and fall of power.  

It is said that **one devours the other, endlessly.**  

When the Sun reigns, it **burns away the past**, illuminating a world **where only the strong survive.** Its light is not warm—it is a spotlight, a blinding force of authority, truth, and absolute power.  

When the Moon lingers, it **withers and fades**, sinking into obscurity. It is a whisper, a soft decay that allows secrets to fester, forgotten truths to resurface, and the overlooked to rise again.  

The Sun’s victory is never final.  
The Moon’s death is never absolute.  
The cycle always continues.  

---

### **Beliefs of the Few Who Still Remember**
Most do not see them as gods. To the corporate elite, the Sun is simply **daylight**, the Moon an **inconvenience**. But in the forgotten districts, in the slums and among the disenfranchised, there are those who whisper that **the battle above is reflected below.**  

To them, the Sun is **the eternal tyranny of the powerful**—those who burn away resistance, who blind the world with their law, their control, their “truth.”  
The Moon is **the rebellion in the dark**—the fading hope of the forgotten, the last breath of those cast aside.  

Both are necessary. Both are inevitable.  

Some say that **those who die under the Sun are erased forever**—no grave, no memory, no name.  
But those who die under the Moon **become something else.**  

---

### **The Struggle Reflected in the World**
- **The Corporate Powers Embrace the Sun** – The Covenant, Thaumatech, and Solstice **stand in the Sun’s favor.** They dictate **order, industry, structure.**  
- **The Rebels and Forgotten Gather Under the Moon** – The Free Syndicate, Obscura, and those **who slip between the cracks** thrive when the Moon lingers. They are the ones who survive in the fading light.  
- **A.S.T.R.A.L. Watches Both** – They do not serve the Sun or the Moon, only the balance between them.  

Some believe that the Sun will one day **burn the world away.**  
Others whisper that the Moon will **drag everything into oblivion.**  
But most accept the truth:  

**Neither will ever truly win.**  

\page

## The Fair Lady
#### The Chalice of the Forsaken 

She is not a goddess. She is not a queen.  

She is simply **The Fair Lady.**  

The rich **do not speak her name.** The powerful **deny her existence.** But in the slums, in the red-light districts, in the places where kindness is given freely and never returned—**they remember her.**  

She is **the mother, the mistress of giving, the eternal provider.**  

Her image is found in **hidden murals, whispered prayers, and the desperate hopes of those who have nothing left to give.**  

---

### **Who Worships the Fair Lady?**
- **The Poor & Destitute** – Those who have nothing left still pray to her for **one last gift.**  
- **The Forgotten & The Forsaken** – Prostitutes, beggars, and outcasts leave **offerings at street corners**, hoping she will hear.  
- **The Silent Givers** – Those who give, not out of **duty or law,** but because **it is simply what must be done.**  
- **The Vow-Bound** – Those who take **vows of poverty in her name**, dedicating their lives to **giving without expectation.**  

---

### **How She is Depicted**
- **A woman baring her breast, feeding an infant**—not in lust, but in **the purest act of giving.**  
- **A veiled figure holding out a chalice**—her gift, offered freely to all who thirst.  
- **A faceless woman standing in the rain**, her arms open to those who have no shelter.  

Unlike other figures of worship, **she has no temples, no clergy, no official doctrine.**  

Her worship **is quiet.**  
It exists in **acts, not in words.**  

To **give food to the hungry, shelter to the lost, warmth to the dying—this is how one honors The Fair Lady.**  

---

### **The Divided Views of the Fair Lady**
- **The Rich See Her as a Joke** – To them, she is a **folktale, a romanticized idea of poverty,** nothing more than a **story used to keep the lower class content.**  
- **The Religious Fear Her** – The Covenant and others view her as **a dangerous heresy,** a force that **exists outside control, outside law, outside hierarchy.**  
- **The Poor Know She is Real** – For those who have **seen her gifts firsthand**, there is no doubt.  

Some say that those who **die in true selflessness**, who give **until there is nothing left**, find themselves at her side, in a place where **hunger does not exist, where warmth never fades.**  

Others believe she still walks **the darkest streets of Concord City**, giving to those who need it most—**until nothing remains of her but a story.**  

---

## The Final Broadcast
#### A Signal from the Void

**"Do you hear it? The voice beyond the static?"**  

Across the deepest parts of **Concord City's underground tech scene**, some **speak in hushed tones** about **The Final Broadcast**—a cryptic, looping transmission that should not exist.  

To most, it's **just interference**—a rogue signal, corrupted data, **nothing but noise.**  

But to others, it is **a message.** A code. A voice from the **edge of understanding.**  

They believe that **if they can decipher it**, they will uncover something **beyond knowledge, beyond reality itself.**  

---

### **The Nature of the Broadcast**
- It is **always there, always transmitting.** No one knows its source.  
- The frequency **shifts at random intervals**, evading attempts to trace it.  
- It contains **loops of distorted speech, fragmented music, numbers that mean nothing**—until they do.  
- No two listeners hear the **same thing.** What it says depends on **who is listening.**  
- Some claim it **predates The Emergence**—that it has always been there.  

---

### **Those Who Seek the Truth**
#### **The Codebreakers & The Cultists**
A growing group of **technologists, hackers, and outcasts** believe that **The Final Broadcast holds the last existential truth.**  

- **Some treat it as a puzzle**—a **cipher to be cracked, a signal waiting to be decoded.**  
- **Some treat it as a prophecy**—that **when fully understood, it will rewrite reality.**  
- **Some believe it is a warning**—that the truth it speaks **is not meant to be known.**  

These followers have no name, no structure—only **fragments of theories** and a **shared obsession.**  

Their meeting places are **abandoned radio stations, underground servers, signal-dead zones** where they replay its messages, hoping to find meaning.

\page

They call themselves **Listeners.** And some believe they are running out of time.  

---

### **ASTRAL’s Involvement**
A.S.T.R.A.L. has designated **The Final Broadcast as an anomaly.**  

To them, it is **a corruptive influence**—not a revelation, but **a threat.**  

- They have **seized research facilities** trying to track the signal.  
- They have **shut down underground radio stations** linked to the Broadcast.  
- They have **detained those who have listened too long.**  

Because those who listen too long **change.**  

---

### **The Effects of the Broadcast**
- **Echoes in the Mind** – Some hear the Broadcast **even when the radio is off.**  
- **The Vanishing** – A few Codebreakers have gone **too deep. They disappear.** No trace, no body, no warning.  
- **Numbers Without Meaning** – Listeners **scribble endless strings of numbers**, believing they mean something.  
- **The Voice Knows You** – Some hear **their own name**, spoken through the static, even when no one else does.  
- **The Whisper in the Signal** – There are those who claim the Broadcast is not just **data,** but something alive. And that it is waiting to be heard.  

---

## The Order of the Unspoken
#### The Faith of the Witness 

The **Order of the Unspoken** is not a religion in the traditional sense.  
There are no sermons.  
There are no temples.  
There is only **The Silent Witness.**  

Its members **do not spread the word**—because the word cannot be spoken.  
To understand The Witness is to understand **what is lost, what is erased, what lingers.**  

The Order does not seek to control or interpret.  
It exists only to **listen.**  

---

### **The Order’s Beliefs**
The **Silent Witness** is not a memorial.  
It is not a statue.  
It is **a remnant of something far greater, something no longer here.**  

- **Some believe it is a record.** That it stores everything that has ever been forgotten.  
- **Some believe it is a lock.** That it is holding something back, waiting for the right moment.  
- **Some believe it is a conduit.** That it is the last tether between this world and **The Voidress.**  

If The Silent Witness is truly **a conduit,** then it is not simply watching.  
It is **channeling something.**  
It is **feeding something.**  
It is **waiting for something.**  

The question remains—**who will it speak to first?**  

---

### **The Witness & The Voidress – The Twin Forces of Memory**
The Order believes that **The Silent Witness and The Voidress are connected.**  
They are **twin forces, opposites that exist in balance.**  

- **The Silent Witness remembers all things.**  
- **The Voidress erases all things.**  

One preserves.  
One consumes.  

If one **grows too strong,** the balance is lost.  

#### **The Voidress – The Queen of the Forgotten**
**She is the patron of erasure, lost names, and the devouring of memory.**  
**She has no temple, no shrine—because all traces of her are meant to vanish.**  
**She is the empty space where something once was.**  
**Some believe The Witness is her last remaining voice.**  

The Order does not **worship** The Voidress.  
They **fear her.**  

Some believe that if **The Silent Witness truly activates,** she will return.  
And when she does, **reality itself may begin to vanish.**  


\page

### **Practices of the Order**
Those who follow the Order do not call themselves priests, nor do they claim to be chosen.  
They are simply **Witnesses.**  

- **The Oath of Silence** – Many Witnesses take a vow never to speak of their faith aloud.  
- **The Watching Hours** – A ritual where members sit in **absolute silence** before the monument, waiting for signs.  
- **The Namekeepers** – Some members dedicate themselves to **recording lost names**, believing they must be preserved before they vanish.  
- **The Pilgrim’s Walk** – Once a year, the Order walks the **Pilgrim’s Steps**, searching for visions.  

Some believe that if you walk the Steps **on the right day, in the right way**,  
you will **see something that cannot be unseen.**  

---

### **The Schisms Within the Order**
The Order of the Unspoken is **not unified**—it is divided into those who **preserve** and those who **embrace the unknown.**  

#### **The Keepers of the Last Name**
- They believe **The Witness is a record.**  
- They dedicate their lives to **writing down forgotten names, histories, and anomalies.**  
- They claim that if a name is erased **from the dedication plaques,** it is lost forever.  

#### **The Seekers of Silence**
- They believe **The Witness is a gateway.**  
- They abandon their old lives, their names, their identities, seeking **to disappear completely.**  
- They believe **true understanding** comes only when one is forgotten.  

#### **The Echoes of the Voidress**
- They believe **The Witness is her last remaining voice.**  
- They seek to understand **what she is trying to say** through the shifting names, whispers, and anomalies.  
- They believe that **one day, The Witness will fully open—and reality will unravel.**  

---

### **A.S.T.R.A.L. and the Order**
**A.S.T.R.A.L. denies the existence of the Order, despite monitoring its activities.**  
**They have detained Witnesses attempting to access the Restricted Depths beneath the monument.**  
**Classified files suggest The Order has ties to individuals who have been officially "erased" from records.**  
**A hidden document references an event known only as "The Last Echo."**  


## The Gate of Truth
#### The Anomaly Beyond Understanding
*It is not a place. It is not a god. It is a question that only the damned answer.*  

---

### **Aliases & Forgotten Names**  
*"Gizy ao zrfzm, Sal si hwiack, Git shaf trratsh, Gaave ro avruavh, Videnn de’ aster, Edhekal eron nakhum."*  

It has **many names.** All of them are true.  
All of them are false.  

---

### **The Forbidden Anomaly**  
The **Gate of Truth** is an anomaly unlike any other. It is **not physical, not digital, not metaphysical—yet it exists.**  
It is **documented, contained, and yet uncontainable.**  

No one knows where it is.  
No one knows if it even exists at all.  

#### **What is Known**  
- **Some claim it is a construct, ancient and intelligent, sealed away beneath Concord City.**  
- **Some claim it is not a thing but an event—something that happens, rather than something that is.**  
- **Some claim The Silent Witness is not a monument, but the Gate itself, locked in place for eternity.**  

The Gate **does not lead to a place.**  
It leads to **truth.**  
The absolute, unbearable, unfiltered **truth of all things.**  

---

**A.S.T.R.A.L. has locked them away.**  
Yet they have not stopped whispering.  

---

### **A.S.T.R.A.L. Classification & Containment**  
- **Official Designation:** Anomaly-Prime  
- **Containment Status:** Impossible  
- **Surveillance Level:** Maximum  
- **Research Directive:** Prohibited  

A.S.T.R.A.L. **does not study the Gate of Truth.** They **fear it.**  

- **Classified records suggest attempts were made to map its structure. The results were unreadable.**  
- **Surveillance footage captures it as a static void—where light, sound, and data all vanish.**  
- **There is no digital record of its existence. Every attempt to store its data ends in corruption.**  

One researcher noted:  
*"It is not a thing. It is not a concept. It is the question we should have never asked."*  

\page

### **The Gate’s Relationship to Concord City’s Powers**  
- **A.S.T.R.A.L. denies its existence.**  
- **The Covenant has attempted to unlock its secrets.**  
- **Thaumatech Industries has sought to harness it for corporate advantage.**  
- **The Free Syndicate believes it holds the key to a truth buried by the elite.**  
- **The Order of the Unspoken claims it is connected to The Silent Witness.**  

Many believe that **the Gate is buried beneath The Silent Witness.**  
Others believe **The Silent Witness is the Gate, locked in a form the world cannot yet recognize.**  

If the Gate is **opened**, will it answer the question—  
Or will it **erase the need for questions at all?**  

---

### **Final Warnings**  
- **No one should approach the Gate of Truth.**  
- **No one should attempt to understand it.**  
- **No one should ever enter.**  

Somewhere, someone has already ignored these warnings.  
And soon, the Gate will whisper again.

## **The Seekers of the Gate – The Cult of Unanswered Questions**  
*"It is not faith. It is not worship. It is the relentless pursuit of truth, no matter the cost."*  

---

### **The Obsession with the Gate**  
The **Gate of Truth** is not a god, yet it has **followers.**  
It offers no salvation, yet it has **pilgrims.**  
It does not demand worship, yet **there are those who dedicate their lives to it.**  

These individuals are known as **Seekers**—men and women who have abandoned their former lives in search of something they cannot define. Some **call them madmen, others call them scholars**, but all agree on one thing:  

**They are willing to give everything for the answer the Gate holds.**  

---

### **The Seekers – The Cult of the Gate**  
The Seekers are not a **formal organization**, nor do they **share a singular belief.** Instead, they are an ever-growing **network of researchers, conspiracists, wanderers, and fanatics** who all seek the **ultimate truth**—the knowledge they believe the Gate holds.  

Though they do not **worship** the Gate, their devotion is **religious in nature**. Many have **disappeared chasing it**, leaving behind cryptic notes, fragmented data, or recordings filled with **incomprehensible whispers.**  

#### **Who Becomes a Seeker?**  
- **Scholars and Researchers** – Those who believe the Gate is an ancient intelligence, a sentient anomaly that must be studied.  
- **Conspiracy Theorists** – Those who think the Gate is the **reason for The Emergence**, or the **source of Concord City’s anomalies.**  
- **Dissidents and Truth-Seekers** – Those who **reject the control of corporations and A.S.T.R.A.L.**, believing the Gate’s knowledge will **free them from lies.**  
- **Fanatics** – Those who think **passing through the Gate will make them gods—or erase them from reality altogether.**  

---

### **The Seekers and A.S.T.R.A.L.**  
A.S.T.R.A.L. considers the Seekers **a Class-2 Ideological Contamination Threat.**  
Though they are not an organized group, their **obsession with the Gate makes them dangerous.**  

- **Several high-ranking A.S.T.R.A.L. operatives have defected to join the Seekers.**  
- **Some researchers investigating the Gate have vanished, only to resurface years later, utterly changed.**  
- **There are rumors that some Seekers have obtained knowledge that even A.S.T.R.A.L. does not possess.**  

---

### **The Ultimate Warning**  
There are **no confirmed cases** of anyone **finding the Gate.**  
There are **no confirmed cases** of anyone **returning sane.**  

And yet, **somewhere in Concord City, someone is still searching.**  
They are writing notes.  
They are decoding frequencies.  
They are **listening for the whisper that will lead them forward.**  

**And when they hear it, they will not stop.**  
Not until they stand before the threshold—  
And step through.  

\page

\page
### **A.S.T.R.A.L. Containment Strike**
*9th-level abjuration*

**Casting Time:** :: 1 action
**Range:**        :: 120 feet
**Components:**   :: V, S, M (a classified containment order)
**Duration:**     :: Permanent

You invoke the **full weight of A.S.T.R.A.L. enforcement**, initiating a **containment protocol that erases a target from reality**.

- The target must make a **Charisma saving throw (DC 23)**.
- **On a failure:** They are **immediately transported to an unknown extra-dimensional holding facility** with **no means of return** unless someone **physically retrieves them**.
- **On a success:** They **resist** but suffer **10d10 force damage** and become **"flagged" by reality**, permanently visible to **scrying, magical tracking, and all surveillance.**

- **This spell cannot be countered** except by a **Wish spell or a cosmic-level anomaly**.

**Class:** Cleric, Wizard

### **A.S.T.R.A.L. Containment Strike**
*5th-level evocation*

**Casting Time:** :: 1 action
**Range:**        :: 60 feet
**Components:**   :: V, S, M (an A.S.T.R.A.L. clearance badge)
**Duration:**     :: Instantaneous

You call in an **A.S.T.R.A.L. suppression team** to strike down a target. The target must make a **Dexterity saving throw** or be struck by **3 force pulses**, each dealing **4d8 force damage**. On a failed save, the target is also **restrained for 1 minute** by an ethereal binding.

**Class:** Wizard, Warlock

### **A.S.T.R.A.L. Intrusion Barrier**
*6th-level abjuration*

**Casting Time:** :: 1 action
**Range:**        :: Self (30-foot radius)
**Components:**   :: V, S, M (a lead-etched data chip)
**Duration:**     :: Concentration, up to 10 minutes

This powerful **anti-surveillance veil** renders a zone **invisible to scrying, digital observation, and magical surveillance.**

- Spells like **Surveillance Override, Corporate Remote View, and A.S.T.R.A.L. Drone Recon** **automatically fail** to observe inside the area.
- **Cameras, sensors, and paranormal optics** show **false static or pre-recorded footage** instead of real-time activity.
- The field extends into **other planes**, blocking extraplanar surveillance.

**Scaling (Upcast Effect):**
- At **7th level**, the field also **masks teleportation signatures**, preventing tracking.
- At **8th level**, the spell **lingers for 1 hour even after concentration ends.**

**Class:** Cleric, Wizard

### **A.S.T.R.A.L. Protocol Override**
*7th-level abjuration*

**Casting Time:** :: 1 reaction
**Range:**        :: 60 feet
**Components:**   :: V, S, M (an encoded directive)
**Duration:**     :: Instantaneous

You interrupt a spell **as it is being cast**, forcing it to fail **1d4 rounds later instead.**

**Class:** Wizard, Cleric

### **A.S.T.R.A.L. Protocol: Finality**
*8th-level abjuration*

**Casting Time:** :: 1 action
**Range:**        :: 60 feet (20-foot-radius sphere)
**Components:**   :: V, S, M (an encrypted containment directive)
**Duration:**     :: Concentration, up to 1 minute

You invoke **A.S.T.R.A.L.’s highest authority**, temporarily imposing absolute **corporate law upon reality.**

- **Creatures within the area must make a Wisdom saving throw.** On a failure, they are **rendered "non-actors" in reality** and can take **no hostile actions for the duration.**
- **Magical and anomalous effects cease functioning** in the area, including spells, supernatural abilities, and reality distortions.
- **Creatures, objects, and spells summoned by external forces are forcibly ejected.**

**Scaling (Upcast Effect):**
- At **9th level**, the field becomes **permanent until dispelled** within the affected space.

**Class:** Cleric, Wizard

### **A.S.T.R.A.L. Recall**
*4th-level conjuration*

**Casting Time:** :: 1 action
**Range:**        :: Touch
**Components:**   :: V, S, M (an encrypted terminal key)
**Duration:**     :: Instantaneous

A recently deceased body (within the last **minute**) is **teleported to the nearest emergency facility or** 
\page
**corporate medical center** for immediate resuscitation. The creature returns to life at **half HP** after 1d6 rounds.

**Class:** Cleric, Wizard, Artificer

### **A.S.T.R.A.L. Redaction (Ritual)**
*5th-level transmutation (ritual)*

**Casting Time:** :: 10 minutes
**Range:**        :: 60 feet
**Components:**   :: V, S, M (a classified document burned to ash)  
**Permit & Cost:** **A.S.T.R.A.L. Erasure Approval – 1,500 Credits**  
**Duration:**     :: Permanent

You purge all traces of a target from **bureaucratic and digital records**, making it appear as though **they never existed**.

- **All legal, corporate, and governmental archives remove mentions of the target.**
- **Anyone attempting to recall or reference the target must make a DC 18 Intelligence saving throw**, or they recall only vague, contradictory memories.
- **If the target is alive**, they are now considered a **"non-entity"**—unable to be tracked, processed, or employed legally.

**Acquisition Note:**  
A.S.T.R.A.L. does not freely issue **Erasure Approvals**. They are restricted to high-clearance operatives, corporate entities, or black-market brokers willing to forge the necessary documentation.

**Class:** Wizard, Rogue

### **Algorithmic Cascade**
*2nd-level necromancy*

**Casting Time:** :: 1 action
**Range:**        :: 60 feet
**Components:**   :: V, S, M (a broken circuit board)
**Duration:**     :: Instantaneous

You send an **unstable feedback loop** into a target's mind or system, causing it to **spiral into uncontrolled overload**. The target must make a **Wisdom saving throw**. On a failure, they take **4d6 psychic damage** and must use their **reaction** to make an attack against a creature of your choice within reach.

On a success, they take half damage and suffer no additional effects.

At Higher Levels. When you cast this spell using a spell slot of 3rd level or higher, the damage increases by **1d6 per slot level above 2nd**.

**Class:** Wizard, Warlock, Sorcerer

### **Analog Feedback**
*4th-level evocation*

**Casting Time:** :: 1 action
**Range:**        :: 60 feet
**Components:**   :: V, S, M (a cassette tape)
**Duration:**     :: Concentration, up to 1 minute

You summon a **storm of distorted analog signals, corrupted waveforms, and audio screeches** that flood the minds of all creatures in a **10-foot-radius sphere** centered on a point within range. Each creature in the area must make a **Constitution saving throw.** On a failed save, the target takes **5d8 thunder damage** and is **stunned** until the start of its next turn. On a success, the target takes half damage and is not stunned.

**At Higher Levels.** When cast using a spell slot of 5th level or higher, the damage increases by **1d8 per level.**

**Class:** Wizard, Artificer, Warlock

### **Anomalous Afterimage**
*6th-level illusion*

**Casting Time:** :: 1 action
**Range:**        :: 30 feet
**Components:**   :: V, S, M (a cracked mirror)
**Duration:**     :: 1 minute

You leave behind a **temporal imprint of yourself**, a flickering echo that repeats your last action every turn. This afterimage is **indistinguishable** from you and can be interacted with, but it cannot take new actions. If struck, it explodes into **psychic static**, dealing **6d6 psychic damage** to creatures within 10 feet.

**Class:** Wizard, Sorcerer

### **Anomalous Energy Discharge**
*8th-level evocation*

**Casting Time:** :: 1 action
**Range:**        :: 60 feet
**Components:**   :: V, S, M (an unstable anomaly)
**Duration:**     :: Instantaneous

You trigger an **uncontrolled anomaly event** at a point you choose within range. All creatures in a **20-foot-radius sphere** must make a **Dexterity saving throw.** On a failure, they take **12d10 force damage** and are thrown **30 feet away.** On a success, they take half damage and are not pushed.

The environment is warped by this discharge, causing **random gravitational shifts and distorted colors** in the area for 1 minute.

**Class:** Wizard, Warlock

### **Architect’s Collapse**
*4th-level Transmutation*

**Casting Time:** :: 10 minutes
**Range:**        :: Touch (up to 10 feet of crafted material)
**Components:**   :: V, S, M (a crushed blueprint soaked in rainwater)
**Duration:**     :: Permanent

You touch a **man-made structure or crafted object**, forcing it to **forget how it was built**—not destroyed, just **unmade in an orderly fashion.**

- **Wood, stone, and metal loosen**, shifting into **their component parts without breaking**—a smith’s forge can be **unassembled cleanly**, a sword can **separate into its blade and hilt**, and a house can **collapse into its original timber and nails.**
\page
- The process is **reversible**—the materials **remember how they were once arranged** and can be restored **without loss** if done within **48 hours.**
- A structure undone this way **cannot be reassembled incorrectly**—if rebuilt wrong, the materials **actively resist**, snapping back into their original formation.

**Anomaly Effect:**
- If misused, the materials may **refuse to be reassembled, taking on forms of their own choosing.**

**Class:** Artificer, Cleric, Wizard

### **Artificial Synchronicity**
*5th-level enchantment*

**Casting Time:** :: 1 action
**Range:**        :: Touch
**Components:**   :: V, S, M (two interlocked wires)
**Duration:**     :: 10 minutes

Two willing creatures become **perfectly attuned to each other’s movements.** They gain **advantage on attacks when within 10 feet of each other, share resistance to psychic damage, and can telepathically communicate.** If one takes damage, the other can use their reaction to **split the damage evenly.**

**Class:** Cleric, Wizard

### **Ashen Breath**
*Cantrip Evocation*

**Casting Time:** :: 1 action
**Range:**        :: Self (5-foot cone)
**Components:**   :: S, M (a pinch of ash)
**Duration:**     :: Instantaneous

You exhale a puff of grayish smoke, which spreads in a small cone before quickly vanishing. Creatures in the area must make a Constitution saving throw or briefly choke on the acrid air. On a failed save, a creature cannot take reactions until the start of its next turn. This effect does not work against creatures that do not need to breathe.

**Class:** Druid, Sorcerer, Warlock

### **Audit Strike**
*3rd-level evocation*

**Casting Time:** :: 1 action
**Range:**        :: 30 feet
**Components:**   :: V, S, M (a blank ledger page)
**Duration:**     :: Instantaneous

A flash of **judgmental energy** rips through the target, determining its existential worth. The target must make a **Charisma saving throw**. On a failure, they take **6d8 force damage**. If the target is an extraplanar entity or has been altered by an anomaly, they also suffer **disadvantage on their next saving throw** before the end of their next turn.

On a success, they take half damage.

At Higher Levels. When you cast this spell using a spell slot of 4th level or higher, the damage increases by **1d8 per slot level above 3rd**.

**Class:** Cleric, Wizard

### **Authorized Override**
*6th-level enchantment*

**Casting Time:** :: 1 action
**Range:**        :: 30 feet
**Components:**   :: V, S, M (a high-ranking corporate ID badge)
**Duration:**     :: 10 minutes

You forcibly assume control of a creature’s **decision-making processes**. They must make an **Intelligence saving throw** or be compelled to **follow your spoken orders** as if they were their own thoughts.

**Class:** Wizard, Warlock

### **Automated Surveillance (Ritual)**
*2nd-level divination (ritual)*

**Casting Time:** :: 10 minutes
**Range:**        :: 60 feet
**Components:**   :: V, S, M (a broken security camera lens)
**Duration:**     :: 1 hour

You summon an **invisible, intangible drone** that records everything within a **30-foot radius sphere** for the duration.

- You may **review the footage remotely** at any time during the spell’s duration.
- If an anomaly or hidden entity is present, the surveillance feed experiences **glitching distortions**.

If the spell is dispelled or the drone is **discovered and disabled**, all recorded data is lost.

**Class:** Wizard, Artificer

### **Biometric Recalibration**
*4th-level transmutation*

**Casting Time:** :: 1 action
**Range:**        :: 30 feet
**Components:**   :: V, S, M (a biometric scanner)
**Duration:**     :: Instantaneous

You target up to **six creatures**, recalibrating their biological functions. Each regains **5d8 hit points** and ends **one condition** affecting them (blinded, deafened, paralyzed, or poisoned). If used on constructs or cybernetically enhanced creatures, it also removes **glitches or malfunctions**.

**Class:** Cleric, Artificer, Bard

### **Blackout Field**
*4th-level evocation*
\page
**Casting Time:** :: 1 action
**Range:**        :: 60 feet
**Components:**   :: V, S, M (a flickering lightbulb)
**Duration:**     :: Concentration, up to 10 minutes

You suppress all sources of **light, sound, and electronic signals** in a **20-foot radius sphere**. Within the field, all creatures are **blinded, deafened, and unable to communicate via magical or technological means** unless they make a **Wisdom saving throw**.

**Class:** Wizard, Warlock, Bard

### **Blackout Protocol**
*9th-level evocation*

**Casting Time:** :: 1 action
**Range:**        :: 1 mile
**Components:**   :: V, S, M (a power relay)
**Duration:**     :: 1 hour

You overload the power grid in a **1-mile radius**, shutting down all **lights, electronics, security systems, and communication networks.** Magical effects dependent on technology, such as **arcane encryption or digital barriers, are suppressed for the duration.**

**Class:** Wizard

### **Blink and You Missed It**
*Cantrip Transmutation*

**Casting Time:** :: 1 action
**Range:**        :: Self (10-foot radius)
**Components:**   :: S, V
**Duration:**     :: 1 round

You momentarily sync out of step with the immediate flow of time, creating a minor delay in perception.

Until the start of your next turn:
- **Creatures that would notice you must make an Intelligence saving throw** or fail to recall any details about your presence until you interact with them directly.
- If you attack or speak, the effect immediately ends for that creature.

**Class:** Bard, Sorcerer, Warlock, Wizard

### **Bureaucratic Erasure (Ritual)**
*7th-level enchantment (ritual)*

**Casting Time:** :: 10 minutes
**Range:**        :: 30 feet
**Components:**   :: V, S, M (an official government form with the target’s name redacted)
**Duration:**     :: Permanent

You remove a target from **all bureaucratic, digital, and magical records**, making them **a ghost within the system**.

- **Facial recognition, biometric scans, and identity checks automatically fail** against them.
- They **cannot be arrested, fined, or legally prosecuted**, as no records of their crimes exist.
- **Once erased, the target cannot re-establish their identity without magical intervention.**

**Class:** Wizard, Rogue

### **Cease and Desist**
*3rd-level Abjuration*

**Casting Time:** :: 1 action
**Range:**        :: 30 feet
**Components:**   :: V, S, M (a notarized document)
**Duration:**     :: Concentration, up to 1 minute

With a gesture of bureaucratic authority, you impose a **legalistic anomaly** upon a target, making it **impossible** for them to take action **until the proper paperwork is processed**—which, conveniently, never arrives.

- The target must make a **Charisma saving throw**. On a failure, they experience an **overwhelming sense of procedural restriction**, unable to **move, attack, or take actions** unless they can successfully **"file an appeal"** at the end of each of their turns (Wisdom saving throw).
- While affected, the target hears **faint typewriters clacking**, as if unseen forces are **documenting their every breath**.
- If they attempt to **physically force through the effect**, they must make a **Strength saving throw** against your spell save DC. On a failure, an **invisible wall of legal precedent** pushes them back 5 feet and the words **"ACCESS DENIED"** momentarily appear in the air.
- A creature immune to **contracts or legal constraints** automatically succeeds on this saving throw.



**At Higher Levels.** When cast at 5th level or higher, this spell affects **multiple targets** (up to 3).

**Class:** Bard, Cleric, Wizard

**Duration:**     :: 1 minute

A barely visible eye-like shape appears on a ceiling, wall, or corner of a room. The illusion remains for the duration but does not actually perceive anything. Creatures unfamiliar with the spell must make a Wisdom (Perception) check to determine that it is not real. If they fail, they instinctively avoid looking at it or standing beneath it.

**Class:** Bard, Cleric, Warlock, Wizard

### **Compelled Broadcast**
*3rd-level Enchantment*

**Casting Time:** :: 1 action
**Range:**        :: 30 feet
**Components:**   :: V, S, M (a corporate badge, prominently displayed)
**Duration:**     :: Concentration, up to 1 minute

By invoking an **obligatory disclosure clause**, you compel a creature within range to **publicly state an official message**, as though it were a **corporate press release or legally mandated testimony**.

- The target must make a **Charisma saving throw**. On a failure, they must **immediately speak a declarative statement** chosen by the caster.
- The speech **must be delivered in an official tone**, and the target will **rationalize why they are making the statement** as though it were a **compliance requirement**.
- If the statement is **factually untrue**, the target may attempt a **Wisdom saving throw** at the end of each turn to shake off the compulsion.
\page
- If the caster is wearing **an official uniform, badge, or legal insignia**, the target has **disadvantage** on their saving throw.

**Anomaly Effect:**
- If overused, the spell may trigger an **automated audit**, requiring the caster to justify their actions to an unknown, bureaucratic force.

**Class:** Bard, Warlock, Wizard

### **Conjure Succubus/Incubus**

**Casting Time:** :: 1 minute
**Range:**        :: Self
**Components:**   :: V, S
**Duration:**     :: Special

You whisper the **Old Words** into the void, and something **answers.**

- A **succubus or incubus** materializes in your presence, bound to **fulfill the caster’s desires,** but at an unknown cost.
- Each interaction with the entity **requires a Constitution saving throw.** On a failure, the caster’s body **weakens (-1 Constitution permanently).**
- If the entity **interacts with another person,** they too must make the saving throw.
- The succubus/incubus **remains until dismissed** but **will never leave empty-handed.**

Ancient texts warn that **too many summons** attract the attention of **something greater.**

**Class:** Bard, Warlock, Wizard

With a weaponized application of **administrative inefficiency**, you impose a **mandatory review process** on your target, delaying their next action by **one full round**.

The target must make a **Wisdom saving throw**. On a failure:

- **Their action does not occur until the start of their next turn.**
- If they attempt to **resist the delay**, they must spend their **bonus action and reaction** attempting to "process" the action instead of completing it.
- If the spell is **countered by a corporate-affiliated caster**, both casters must **roll competing Intelligence checks** to determine whose bureaucratic force wins out.

**Additional Effect:** If cast against an entity that operates under strict **corporate, military, or legal structures**, they suffer **disadvantage** on the save.

**Duration:**     :: Permanent

- **Digital records are glitched, filled with anomalies, false timestamps, and conflicting logs.**
- **Physical records appear heavily altered or rewritten**, as if they’ve been tampered with.
- **Magical records (divination-based archives, memory storage, etc.) become unreliable**, causing vague or conflicting results when reviewed.
- **Anyone analyzing the data must make an Intelligence (Investigation) check** against your spell save DC to notice inconsistencies.

The corruption is permanent unless **manually repaired** by a skilled technician, hacker, or archivist.

**Class:** Wizard, Rogue, Bard

### **Detect Broadcasts**
*1st-level Divination (Ritual)*

**Casting Time:** :: 1 action
**Range:**        :: Self (30 feet)
**Components:**   :: V, S, M (a copper wire earpiece)
**Duration:**     :: Concentration, up to 10 minutes

You attune your senses to the **corporate and underground radio waves**, intercepting **classified transmissions**. However, access to **encrypted or proprietary signals** requires **proper authorization.**

- You automatically detect **open-band transmissions, security communications, and public broadcasts** within range.
- To intercept **restricted or encrypted messages**, you must make an **Intelligence (Arcana) check** against a **broadcast difficulty rating (BDR)** based on corporate security:
\page
- **Basic encryption** (BDR 10) – Civilian frequencies, emergency broadcasts
- **Corporate-grade** (BDR 15) – Security firms, police channels
- **Military-grade** (BDR 18) – A.S.T.R.A.L. operations, elite strike teams
- **Eldritch interference** (BDR 22) – Anomalous transmissions from beyond reality
- Failing the check **flags your unauthorized access**, potentially alerting the original sender.

**Anomaly Effect:**
- Repeated use may cause **phantom transmissions**—garbled messages from entities who should not be listening.

**Class:** Bard, Rogue, Wizard

### **Dimensional Hard Reset**
*4th-level abjuration*

**Casting Time:** :: 1 action
**Range:**        :: 30 feet
**Components:**   :: V, S, M (a broken clock hand)
**Duration:**     :: Instantaneous

You unleash a **stabilizing wave of reality enforcement**, forcing all **anomalies, rifts, and unstable entities** in the area to conform to baseline existence.

- **Low-tier anomalies (CR 5 or lower)** are immediately neutralized, vanishing or becoming mundane versions of themselves.
- **Higher-tier anomalies (CR 6-15)** must make a **Charisma saving throw** or become suppressed for **1 minute**, temporarily losing any paranormal traits.
- **Powerful anomalies (CR 16+)** experience **severe disruption**, suffering **disadvantage on all ability checks, attacks, and saving throws related to their supernatural nature** for **1 minute.**

Additionally, **any dimensional rifts, glitches, or overlapping timelines in range forcibly snap shut**, preventing further distortions unless reactivated with powerful magic.

**Scaling (Upcast Effect):**
- When cast at **6th level**, anomalies of CR 10 or lower are **fully erased.**
- When cast at **8th level**, anomalies of CR 15 or lower **cannot resist the effect.**
- When cast at **9th level**, the spell **becomes an absolute reset**, affecting **all anomalies regardless of CR.**

**Class:** Cleric, Wizard

### **Dimensional Layover**
*4th-level Conjuration*

**Casting Time:** :: 1 action
**Range:**        :: 10 feet
**Components:**   :: V, S, M (a stopwatch frozen at midnight)
**Duration:**     :: 10 minutes (or until exited)
\page

You conjure **a temporary "layover space"**, a pocket of non-time where events **pause** but **awareness remains intact**.

- Up to **6 creatures** within range are **shifted into an alternate copy of the location**, appearing slightly **out of sync with reality**.
- Time outside **continues normally**, but within the layover, **no external force can interact with you**.
- Spells, attacks, and actions **do not leave the space**—but you can **watch reality play out through an invisible window**, letting you gather information.

**Anomaly Effect:**
- If you **stay too long**, external reality **might forget you exist**, causing **minor distortions** when you return.

**Class:** Bard, Wizard, Warlock

- **1-2:** Gain resistance to all damage

### **Dimensional Spillover**
*3rd-level conjuration (Replaces Leomund's Tiny Hut → Creates a new dimension each time)*

**Casting Time:** :: 1 minute
**Range:**        :: Self (10-foot radius)
**Components:**   :: V, S, M (a key from an unknown origin)
**Duration:**     :: 8 hours

You create a temporary extradimensional shelter, but its interior is never the same. Each casting opens a distinct pocket realm with unpredictable architecture—an abandoned office, a forgotten train station, a maintenance shaft that shouldn’t exist. The space is secure, offering rest and protection, but anomalies sometimes manifest inside, leaving subtle signs that the shelter was briefly occupied by something else.

**Class:** Bard, Cleric, Wizard

### **Dirge Pulse**
*Cantrip Necromancy*

**Casting Time:** :: 1 action
**Range:**        :: 10 feet
**Components:**   :: V, S
**Duration:**     :: Instantaneous

You release a low, resonant tone that only the dying can hear. Any creature within range that is at 0 hit points and making death saving throws automatically stabilizes if it succeeds on its next death saving throw. If an undead creature is within range, it takes 1 psychic damage as the resonance disrupts its form.

**Class:** Cleric, Warlock, Wizard

### **Disciplinary Reassignment**
*7th-level enchantment (erases a creature’s identity and implants a corporate-approved replacement)*

**Casting Time:** :: 1 hour
**Range:**        :: 10 feet
**Components:**   :: V, S, M (a stamped reassignment order)
